Consensus on Prophetic Inerrancy from Kufr and the Azariqa Exception
Consensus on prophetic inerrancy from kufr, with Azariqa exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the consensus on prophets' inerrancy from kufr and the dissenting view of the Azariqa sect.

Core Idea
The ummah agrees prophets are immune from kufr; only the Azariqa disagree.

This passage addresses the question of prophetic inerrancy specifically regarding kufr (disbelief). After establishing the consensus of the Muslim community that prophets are protected from kufr both before and after their prophethood, the author notes the exception of the Azariqa, a subgroup of the Khawarij. Their extreme position, equating all sins with kufr, leads them to contradict the consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the author's concise style and the logical flow from classification to consensus to exception.
2
Identify the consensus and exception
Find the statement of consensus: 'أجمعت الأمة على عصمتهم منه'. Then find the exception: 'غير أن الأزارقة...'. Reflect on how the exception is framed as a departure from the consensus.
The Azariqa are a specific subgroup of the Khawarij, not the entire group.
3
Analyse the Azariqa's reasoning
The text says the Azariqa allow sins on prophets, and since they consider every sin as kufr, they necessarily allow kufr. Trace their logic and consider why this contradicts the consensus.
This connects to the broader debate on defining kufr and the boundaries of prophetic inerrancy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما سائر الذنوب يعني به ما الكذب في التبليغ فهي إما كفر أو غيره من المعاصي . وأما الكفر فأجمعت الأمة على عصمتهم منه قبل النبوة وبعدها ولا خلاف لأحد منهم في ذلك غير أن الأزارقة من الخوارج جوزوا عليهم الذنب وكل ذنب عندهم كفر فلزمهم تجویز الكفر، بل يحكى عنهم أنهم قالوا بجواز بعثة نبي علم الله تعالى أنه يكفر بعد نبوته.
And as for the rest of sins—meaning by that falsehood in conveying—they are either kufr or other than that of acts of disobedience. And as for kufr, the ummah is agreed upon their inerrancy from it before prophethood and after it, and there is no disagreement from anyone concerning that, except that the Azariqa of the Khawarij allowed sins upon them, and every sin according to them is kufr, so they are obliged to allow kufr. Rather, it is narrated from them that they said it is permissible to send a prophet whom God knows will disbelieve after his prophethood.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on sins other than falsehood in conveying the message, classifying them as either kufr or other sins. It then notes the consensus of the Muslim community that prophets are inerrant from kufr both before and after their prophethood. The only dissenting group mentioned is the Azariqa sect of the Khawarij, who hold that all sins are kufr, and since they allow sins in general for prophets, they consequently allow kufr. An extreme view attributed to them is that God can send a prophet knowing that he will later disbelieve.

Refutation of Shia taqiyya using two arguments.

Learning Objective

Core Idea
Taqiyya for prophets would destroy the very purpose of prophethood.

The author directly challenges a controversial Shia doctrine concerning taqiyya. He argues that permitting prophets to outwardly deny their faith under threat would contradict their mission. This passage shows why such a practice is rationally and prophetically untenable.

Identify the two main arguments

The first is a logical consequence, the second is a historical example.

Reflect on the counterexamples

Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage refutes the Shia view that prophets may outwardly display kufr under extreme duress (taqiyya). The author argues that such a practice is absolutely false because it would lead to the complete concealment of the call and abandonment of conveying the message. In fact, the time of greatest need for taqiyya would be during the initial propagation of the message when followers are few and opponents many, but prophets did not resort to it. Furthermore, the examples of Abraham and Moses, who openly called their people despite severe threats from Nimrod and Pharaoh, serve as a refutation of the Shia claim.

Classification of Non-Kufr Sins
Enumeration of four categories of non-kufr sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four-fold classification of non-kufr sins according to the author: major/minor, deliberate/forgetful, and before/after prophethood.

Core Idea
Non-kufr sins are classified by gravity and intent, with further division by timing relative to prophethood.

Before delving into the debate on prophetic inerrancy, the author establishes a clear taxonomy of sins that are not kufr. This classification helps frame the discussion about what is possible or impossible for prophets. The passage below defines four categories based on the sin's magnitude, the agent's intent, and the temporal context.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the four categories
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the two binary distinctions: major/minor and deliberate/forgetful, each multiplied by before/after prophethood. Count the four resulting divisions.
The text explicitly states 'the divisions are four'.
2
Understand the significance of the classification
Ask yourself why this classification matters for the subsequent discussion on major sins deliberately. It sets the stage for focusing on one specific type: major sins committed deliberately after prophethood.
3
Reflect on the completeness
Consider whether all combinations are covered. The text implies a complete enumeration: 2 (gravity) × 2 (intent) × 2 (timing) = 8, but the author says four? Actually it's four because timing is applied after the first split? The text says 'each of them is either before the mission or after it' meaning for each of the four? It's ambiguous. The commentary will clarify.
The author lists four combinations: major deliberate, major forgetful, minor deliberate, minor forgetful, and then each is either before or after mission, effectively 8 subcategories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما غير الكفر فإما كبائر أو صغائر وكل منهما إما أن يصدر عمداً وإما أن يصدر سهواً فالأقسام أربعة وكل واحد منها إما قبل البعثة أو بعدها ( أما الكبائر ) أي صدورها عمداً ( فمنعه الجمهور من المحققين والأئمة ولم يخالف فيه إلا الحشوية ( والأكثر) من المانعين ( على امتناعه سمعاً ) قال القاضي والمحققون من الأشاعرة: إن العصمة فيما وراء التبليغ غير واجبة عقلاً إذ لا دلالة للمعجزة عليه فامتناع الكبائر عمداً مستفاد من السمع وإجماع الأمة قبل ظهور المخالفين في ذلك ( وقالت المعتزلة : بناء على أصولهم الفاسدة في التحسين والتقبيح العقليين ووجوب رعاية الصلاح والأصلح . ( يمتنع ذلك عقلاً لأن صدور الكبائر عنهم عمداً يوجب سقوط هيبتهم عن القلوب وانحطاط رتبتهم في أعين الناس فيؤدي إلى النفرة عنهم وعدم الانقياد لهم ويلزم منه إفساد الخلائق وترك استصلاحهم وهو خلاف مقتضى العقل والحكمة.
And as for other than kufr, they are either major sins (kaba'ir) or minor sins (sagha'ir), and each of them either occurs deliberately or occurs forgetfully; thus the divisions are four, and each one of them is either before the mission or after it. (As for major sins) i.e., their occurrence deliberately—the majority of verifiers and imams prohibited it, and none dissented except the Hashawiyya. And most of the prohibitors (hold) its impossibility by revelation (sam'). Al-Qadi and the verifiers among the Ash'aris said: Inerrancy beyond conveying the message is not rationally necessary, since there is no indication from the miracle for it, so the impossibility of major sins deliberately is derived from revelation and the consensus of the ummah before the appearance of dissenters on that. And the Mu'tazila said—based on their corrupt principles of rational good and evil and the obligation to observe what is beneficial and most beneficial—that it is rationally impossible, because the occurrence of major sins from them deliberately would cause the fall of their awe from hearts and the degradation of their rank in people's eyes, leading to aversion from them and lack of submission to them, and from that follows the corruption of creation and the abandonment of their reform, which contradicts the dictates of reason and wisdom.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage classifies non-kufr sins into major and minor, and each can be deliberate or forgetful, before or after prophethood—making four categories. The focus then turns to major sins committed deliberately. The majority of scholars (excluding the Hashawiyya) forbid them. The Ash'ari position, represented by al-Qadi and the verifiers, holds that inerrancy regarding such sins is not rationally necessary because the miracle does not cover it; rather, it is established by revelation (sam') and consensus. The Mu'tazila, however, argue from their principles of rational good and evil that it is rationally impossible, because such sins would undermine the prophets' authority and lead to the corruption of society, which contradicts reason and divine wisdom.

Key Terms
كبائر
صغائر
عمد
سهو

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Two
B) Four
C) Eight
D) Six

Key Takeaway
Non-kufr sins are classified into four basic types (major/minor × deliberate/forgetful), each further divided by timing relative to prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

The Debate on Major Sins Deliberately
Presentation of Ash'ari and Mu'tazili arguments on major sins deliberately.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari and Mu'tazili positions on the possibility of prophets committing major sins deliberately, and their respective proofs.

Core Idea
Ash'aris rely on revelation for inerrancy beyond conveying the message; Mu'tazila argue from rational good and evil.

After classifying sins, the author turns to a key dispute: can a prophet commit a major sin deliberately? The majority of scholars, including the Ash'aris, maintain it is impossible by revelation. The Mu'tazila, however, claim it is rationally impossible based on their principles. This passage presents both views with their reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two opposing views
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Note the Ash'ari position: major sins deliberately are impossible by revelation (sam') and consensus. Then the Mu'tazili position: it is rationally impossible because it would undermine prophetic authority.
2
Understand the Ash'ari reasoning
The Ash'aris argue that inerrancy in matters beyond conveying the message is not rationally necessary because the miracle does not prove it. Instead, they rely on revealed texts and the consensus of the community before dissenters appeared.
The text mentions al-Qadi and the verifiers among the Ash'aris.
3
Understand the Mu'tazili reasoning
The Mu'tazila base their argument on rational good and evil ('tahsin wa taqbih) and the obligation to do what is beneficial. If a prophet commits a major sin, people would lose trust, leading to aversion and disobedience, corrupting society—which contradicts wisdom.
The author dismisses their principles as 'corrupt' (fasida).
4
Compare the two approaches
Contrast the foundations: Ash'ari reliance on revelation vs. Mu'tazili reliance on reason. Consider how each defines the scope of prophetic inerrancy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما غير الكفر فإما كبائر أو صغائر وكل منهما إما أن يصدر عمداً وإما أن يصدر سهواً فالأقسام أربعة وكل واحد منها إما قبل البعثة أو بعدها ( أما الكبائر ) أي صدورها عمداً ( فمنعه الجمهور من المحققين والأئمة ولم يخالف فيه إلا الحشوية ( والأكثر) من المانعين ( على امتناعه سمعاً ) قال القاضي والمحققون من الأشاعرة: إن العصمة فيما وراء التبليغ غير واجبة عقلاً إذ لا دلالة للمعجزة عليه فامتناع الكبائر عمداً مستفاد من السمع وإجماع الأمة قبل ظهور المخالفين في ذلك ( وقالت المعتزلة : بناء على أصولهم الفاسدة في التحسين والتقبيح العقليين ووجوب رعاية الصلاح والأصلح . ( يمتنع ذلك عقلاً لأن صدور الكبائر عنهم عمداً يوجب سقوط هيبتهم عن القلوب وانحطاط رتبتهم في أعين الناس فيؤدي إلى النفرة عنهم وعدم الانقياد لهم ويلزم منه إفساد الخلائق وترك استصلاحهم وهو خلاف مقتضى العقل والحكمة.
And as for other than kufr, they are either major sins (kaba'ir) or minor sins (sagha'ir), and each of them either occurs deliberately or occurs forgetfully; thus the divisions are four, and each one of them is either before the mission or after it. (As for major sins) i.e., their occurrence deliberately—the majority of verifiers and imams prohibited it, and none dissented except the Hashawiyya. And most of the prohibitors (hold) its impossibility by revelation (sam'). Al-Qadi and the verifiers among the Ash'aris said: Inerrancy beyond conveying the message is not rationally necessary, since there is no indication from the miracle for it, so the impossibility of major sins deliberately is derived from revelation and the consensus of the ummah before the appearance of dissenters on that. And the Mu'tazila said—based on their corrupt principles of rational good and evil and the obligation to observe what is beneficial and most beneficial—that it is rationally impossible, because the occurrence of major sins from them deliberately would cause the fall of their awe from hearts and the degradation of their rank in people's eyes, leading to aversion from them and lack of submission to them, and from that follows the corruption of creation and the abandonment of their reform, which contradicts the dictates of reason and wisdom.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage classifies non-kufr sins into major and minor, and each can be deliberate or forgetful, before or after prophethood—making four categories. The focus then turns to major sins committed deliberately. The majority of scholars (excluding the Hashawiyya) forbid them. The Ash'ari position, represented by al-Qadi and the verifiers, holds that inerrancy regarding such sins is not rationally necessary because the miracle does not cover it; rather, it is established by revelation (sam') and consensus. The Mu'tazila, however, argue from their principles of rational good and evil that it is rationally impossible, because such sins would undermine the prophets' authority and lead to the corruption of society, which contradicts reason and divine wisdom.

Key Terms

عمد
سمع
تحسين وتقبيح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Ash'aris deny any rational basis for prophetic inerrancy.
Correction: Ash'aris do accept rational necessity for inerrancy in conveying the message, but for other actions they rely on revelation.

Checkpoint
According to the Ash'ari view in the text, what is the basis for forbidding major sins deliberately?
A) Rational necessity
B) Revelation and consensus
C) The miracle directly
D) The Mu'tazila argument

Key Takeaway
The Ash'aris hold that major sins deliberately are forbidden by revelation, while the Mu'tazila argue that reason alone suffices to prohibit them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you learn about a prophet's sinlessness, do you feel more reassured by a rational proof (like the Mu'tazila argument) or by a revealed text (like the Ash'ari reliance on revelation)? Which do you actually trust more in your own heart, and why?
?
The Mu'tazila argue that a major sin would cause people's awe to fall and lead to rejection of the message. Think of someone whose spiritual advice you value. If you saw them commit a major sin, would your confidence in their words collapse? What does that reveal about the foundation of your trust?
?
The Ash'aris say that inerrancy beyond conveying the message is not rationally necessary—only revelation tells us prophets are protected from major sins. Does your faith in the Prophet (peace be upon him) rest more on rational arguments or on the Qur'an and Sunnah? Examine your own belief: is it built on evidence from revelation or on your own reasoning?

Major Sins by Forgetfulness and Minor Sins Deliberately
Discussion of major sins by forgetfulness and minor sins deliberately

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly positions on prophets committing major sins by forgetfulness or interpretive error, and on committing minor sins deliberately, along with the author's chosen view and a rebuttal to a Mu'tazilite argument.

Core Idea
Prophets are protected from sin, but scholars differed on major sins by mistake and minor sins on purpose.

This passage continues the discussion on prophetic infallibility, addressing two controversial cases: whether a prophet could commit a major sin by forgetfulness or interpretive error, and whether a minor sin could be committed intentionally. The author presents the majority views and the selected position, along with a rebuttal to a Mu'tazilite argument that major sins cause loss of awe.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once to get a feel for the flow, then read the literal translation. Notice the two distinct rulings and the marginal notes.
The text includes a digression on the term 'al-Hashawiyya' and a response to the loss-of-awe argument.
2
Identify the two rulings
The passage addresses (1) major sins by forgetfulness/interpretive error, and (2) minor sins deliberately. For each, note the majority view and the author's stance.
For the first, the majority permitted it, but the chosen view is opposite. For the second, the majority permitted it except al-Jubba'i.
3
Understand the author's chosen view
The phrase 'al-mukhtar khilafuhu' indicates the author's preference against the majority on the first issue. This is an important teaching point.
This shows that the author does not simply follow the majority but exercises independent judgment.
4
Examine the rebuttal to the Mu'tazilite argument
The marginal note responds to the claim that major sins cause loss of awe. The reply distinguishes between apparent loss and real loss, and notes that even secretly committed major sins affect awe.
This rebuttal is relevant to the discussion of the effects of sin on prophetic status.

Then concerning them: His saying: (except the Hashawiyya) with a fatha on the shin, attributed to Hashawiyya on the pattern of fa'ula, and it is a village in Khurasan. His saying: (would cause the fall of their awe) it is replied to them that the fall is in appearance and occurrence, and it does not necessarily entail it, unless it is said: the fall of awe is specific to the major sin even if it occurs secretly.

Commentary
This passage covers two remaining categories: major sins by forgetfulness or interpretive error, and minor sins deliberately. The majority permitted both, but the author notes that the chosen view is contrary to the permissibility of major sins by forgetfulness. A marginal note explains that 'al-Hashawiyya' refers to a village in Khurasan. Another marginal note addresses the Mu'tazila argument that major sins cause loss of awe: it responds that the loss is only in appearance and not necessarily real, unless one specifies that loss of awe is specific to major sins even if done secretly.

?

The Fourfold Classification and Intentional Major Sins
Enumeration of sin categories and the first debated category.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourfold classification of sins and the debate over whether prophets can commit major sins intentionally.

Core Idea
The permissibility of intentional major sins is rejected by most scholars, but for different reasons.

The author begins by establishing a clear taxonomy of sins: major vs. minor, intentional vs. unintentional, and before or after prophethood. He then dives into the first category—intentional major sins—and reports the positions of the majority, the Hashwiyya dissenters, the Ash'ari rationalists, and the Mu'tazila. This passage sets the stage for the entire discussion on prophetic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the classification
Start by reading the Arabic passage that classifies sins into four categories. Notice how the author uses 'إما... أو' to enumerate the possibilities.
2
Identify the first position
The passage then states that the majority of investigators and imams forbid intentional major sins, with only the Hashwiyya dissenting. Highlight the phrases that indicate consensus and the exception.
The term 'الحشوية' is explained in a later note.
3
Analyze the Ash'ari argument
Al-Qadi and the Ash'ari investigators argue that infallibility beyond conveying the message is not rationally obligatory. Understand the distinction between rational ('aql) and scriptural (sam') evidence.
4
Compare with the Mu'tazila argument
The Mu'tazila argue rationally that intentional major sins would destroy the prophet's authority, leading to aversion. Compare their approach to the Ash'ari scriptural approach.
The marginal note at the end of the passage critiques the Mu'tazila argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما غير الكفر فإما كبائر أو صغائر وكل منهما إما أن يصدر عمداً وإما أن يصدر سهواً فالأقسام أربعة وكل واحد منها إما قبل البعثة أو بعدها أما الكبائر أي صدورها عمداً فمنعه الجمهور من المحققين والأئمة ولم يخالف فيه إلا الحشوية والأكثر من المانعين على امتناعه سمعاً قال القاضي والمحققون من الأشاعرة: إن العصمة فيما وراء التبليغ غير واجبة عقلاً إذ لا دلالة للمعجزة عليه فامتناع الكبائر عمداً مستفاد من السمع وإجماع الأمة قبل ظهور المخالفين في ذلك وقالت المعتزلة : بناء على أصولهم الفاسدة في التحسين والتقبيح العقليين ووجوب رعاية الصلاح والأصلح . يمتنع ذلك عقلاً لأن صدور الكبائر عنهم عمداً يوجب سقوط هيبتهم عن القلوب وانحطاط رتبتهم في أعين الناس فيؤدي إلى النفرة عنهم وعدم الانقياد لهم ويلزم منه إفساد الخلائق وترك استصلاحهم وهو خلاف مقتضى العقل والحكمة وأما صدورها عنهم سهوا أو على سبيل الخطأ في التأويل فجوزه الأكثرون والمختار خلافه وأما الصغائر عمداً فجوزه الجمهور إلا الجبائي فإنه ذهب إلى أنه لا يجوز صدور الصغيرة إلا بطريق السهو أو الخطأ في التأويل وهذا التجويز منهم إنما هو فيما ليس من صغائر الخسة كما ستعرفه وأما صدور الصغائر سهوا فهو جائز اتفاقا بين أكثر أصحابنا وأكثر المعتزلة إلا الصغائر الخسية وهي ما تلحق فاعلها بالأراذل والسفل والحكم عليه بالخسة ودناءه الهمة كسرقة حبة أو القمة فإنها لا تجوز أصلاً لا عمداً ولا سهواً والاتفاق المذكور إنما هو فيما ليس منها كنظرة وكلمة سفه نادرة في خصام وقال الجاحظ : يجوز أن غير صغار الخسة سهواً بشرط أن ينبهوا عليه فينتهوا عنه وقد تبعه فيه يصدر عنهم كثير من المتأخرين من المعتزلة كالنظام والأصم وجعفر بن بشر وبه نقول نحن معاشر الأشاعرة . هذا كله بعد الوحي والاتصاف بالنبوة وأما قبله فقال الجمهور : أي أكثر أصحابنا وجمع من المعتزلة لا يمتنع أن يصدر عنهم كبيرة إذ لا دلالة للمعجزة عليه أي على امتناع الكبيرة قبل البعثة ولا حكم للعقل بامتناعها ولا دلالة سمعية عليه أيضاً وقال أكثر المعتزلة : تمتنع الكبيرة وإن تاب منها لأنه أي الكبيرة يوجب النفرة عمن ارتكبها وهي تمنع عن اتباعه فتفوت مصلحة البعثة ومنهم من منع عما ينفر الطباع عن متابعتهم مطلقاً أي سواء لم يكن ذنباً لهم أو كان كعهر الأمهات إي كونها زانيات والفجور في الآباء ودناءتهم واسترذالهم والصغائر الخسيسة دون غيرها من الصغائر . وقالت الروافض : لا يجوز عليهم صغيرة ولا كبيرة لا عمداً ولا سهواً ولا خطأ في التأويل بل هم مبرؤون عنها قبل الوحي فكيف بعد الوحي.
قوله : (إلا) الحشوية) بفتح الشين منسوبة إلى حشوية على وزن فعولة وهي قرية من قرى خراسان .
قوله : ( يوجب سقوط هيبتهم يرد عليهم أن السقوط في الظهور والصدور وغير مستلزم إياه . اللهم إلا أن يقال : سقوط الهيبة خاصة الكبيرة ولو صدرت سرا .
As for other than disbelief, it is either major sins or minor sins, and each of them is either committed intentionally or unintentionally. So the divisions are four, and each one is either before the mission or after it. As for major sins — i.e., committing them intentionally — the majority of the investigators and imams forbade it, and only the Hashwiyya differed. And most of those who forbid (rely on) its impossibility being derived from revelation. Al-Qadi and the investigators among the Ash'aris said: Infallibility beyond the matter of conveying (the message) is not rationally obligatory, for the miracle does not indicate it. So the impossibility of major sins intentionally is derived from revelation and the consensus of the community before the appearance of the objectors in that. The Mu'tazila said, based on their corrupt principles of rational (determination of) good and evil and the obligation to observe what is beneficial and most beneficial: That is rationally impossible because committing major sins by them intentionally leads to the loss of their awe in hearts and the lowering of their rank in people's eyes, resulting in aversion to them and lack of submission to them, and it entails corrupting creation and abandoning their cultivation, which is contrary to the requirement of reason and wisdom. As for their committing them unintentionally or by mistake in interpretation, the majority permitted it, but the chosen view is contrary. As for minor sins intentionally, the majority permitted them except al-Jubba'i, for he held that a minor sin is not permissible except by way of oversight or mistake in interpretation. This permission from them is only regarding what is not among the lowly minor sins, as you will come to know. As for committing minor sins unintentionally, it is permissible by agreement between most of our companions and most of the Mu'tazila, except the lowly minor sins, which are what place the doer among the lowly and base and pass judgment on him of lowness and meanness of spirit, like stealing a grain or a morsel — these are absolutely impermissible, whether intentionally or unintentionally. The aforementioned agreement is only regarding what is not among them, like a glance or a rare foolish word in an argument. Al-Jahiz said: It is permissible that (sins) other than the lowly minor sins (be committed) unintentionally, provided that they are warned and desist. Many later Mu'tazila followed him, such as al-Nazzam, al-Asamm, and Ja'far ibn Bashshar. And we — the Ash'ari community — say the same. All this is after revelation and the attribution of prophethood. As for before it, the majority — i.e., most of our companions and a group of the Mu'tazila — said: It is not impossible for a major sin to occur from them, for the miracle does not indicate its impossibility before the mission, nor does reason rule its impossibility, nor is there any scriptural evidence for it either. Most of the Mu'tazila said: The major sin is impossible even if he repents from it, because it causes aversion to the one who committed it, and that prevents following him, thus the benefit of the mission is lost. And some of them forbade what repels natural dispositions from following them absolutely — i.e., whether it is a sin for them or not — like the unchastity of mothers (i.e., they are adulteresses), and lasciviousness in fathers, and their baseness and vileness, and the lowly minor sins, not other minor sins. The Rawafid said: No minor or major sin is permissible for them, whether intentionally, unintentionally, or by mistake in interpretation; rather, they are innocent of them before revelation, so how (could they sin) after revelation? His statement: 'except the Hashwiyya' — with a fatha on the shin, attributed to Hashwiyya on the pattern of fa'ula, and it is a village in Khorasan. His statement: 'leads to the loss of their awe' — it is objected against them that the loss in appearance and occurrence does not necessitate it. However, it could be said: The loss of awe is specific to the major sin even if it occurs secretly.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive classification of sins and the positions of various theological groups on whether prophets can commit them. The author begins by dividing sins into major (kaba'ir) and minor (sagha'ir), each either intentional ('amdan) or unintentional (sahw), resulting in four categories, each considered before or after prophethood. For major sins committed intentionally, the majority (Jumhur) of investigators and imams forbid it, with only the Hashwiyya dissenting. The Ash'ari position is that this impossibility is derived from revelation (sam') not reason, as the miracle only guarantees infallibility in conveying the message. The Mu'tazila, based on their rationalist principles, argue it is rationally impossible because it would destroy the prophet's authority. For major sins unintentionally, most permit it but the preferred view opposes. For minor sins intentionally, most permit except al-Jubba'i. For minor sins unintentionally, there is agreement except for 'lowly' (khissiya) sins that degrade the doer, which are absolutely forbidden. Al-Jahiz and others allow non-lowly minor sins unintentionally with warning. The Ash'aris follow this view. Then the author discusses before prophethood: the majority do not consider major sins impossible, while most Mu'tazila do. The Rawafid (Shi'a) hold absolute infallibility even before prophethood. Two marginal notes clarify the term 'Hashwiyya' and discuss the objection that the loss of awe is not necessarily entailed by a secret sin.

كبائر
صغائر
عمد
سهو
قبل البعثة
بعد البعثة
الحشوية
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that all scholars agree that prophets cannot commit any sin at all.
Correction: The passage shows that the majority only forbids intentional major sins; even among them, the basis differs (revelation vs. reason).

Checkpoint
According to Al-Qadi and the Ash'ari investigators, why is the impossibility of intentional major sins not rationally obligatory?
A) Because reason cannot judge good and evil
B) Because the miracle does not indicate infallibility beyond conveying the message
C) Because the consensus of the community is sufficient
D) Because the Hashwiyya oppose it

Key Takeaway
Intentional major sins by prophets are forbidden by most scholars, but the Ash'aris base this on revelation while the Mu'tazila base it on reason.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Reflect on why the Ash'aris and Mu'tazila both reject this possibility, yet from different foundations. Which foundation resonates more with your own heart—revelation or reason? What does your answer reveal about the basis of your own faith?
?
The passage states that intentional major sins would lead to a loss of awe and submission in the eyes of people. Think of a person you deeply respect. How would a major sin on their part affect your respect? How does this mirror the divine wisdom in preserving prophetic authority? Are there areas in your life where you have rationalized sin away, similar to the Mu'tazila's rational approach? What would it mean to submit to revelation instead?
?
The Mu'tazila argue that allowing sins contradicts reason and wisdom (خلاف مقتضى العقل والحكمة). Have you ever found yourself justifying a sin by calling it 'reasonable' or 'necessary'? How does the Ash'ari reliance on revelation over human reason challenge your own moral decision-making? Commit today to one specific area where you will prioritize divine command over your own reasoning.

Unintentional Major Sins and Minor Sins, Including Lowly Sins
Continuation of the classification: unintentional major, minor sins, and lowly minor sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the positions on prophets committing major sins unintentionally, minor sins intentionally, minor sins unintentionally, and the special category of lowly minor sins.

Core Idea
Most scholars permit minor sins unintentionally, but lowly sins that degrade the prophet are absolutely forbidden.

After discussing intentional major sins, the author turns to less severe categories: major sins committed by accident, minor sins both intentional and unintentional, and the unique category of lowly minor sins (صغائر الخسة). He reports the views of various scholars, including al-Jubba'i, al-Jahiz, and the Ash'ari position. This lesson clarifies the nuanced spectrum of opinions on prophetic fallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read about unintentional major sins
The passage says most scholars permit major sins committed unintentionally, but the preferred view (المختار) opposes. Note the difference between majority opinion and the chosen one.
2
Analyze minor sins intentionally
Most permit them except al-Jubba'i, who only allows them if unintentional or mistaken. Understand the distinction.
The permission excludes lowly minor sins.
3
Examine minor sins unintentionally
Most companions and Mu'tazila permit them, but lowly minor sins (like stealing a grain) are absolutely impermissible. Note the examples given.
4
Learn al-Jahiz's and the Ash'ari view
Al-Jahiz allows non-lowly minor sins unintentionally if warned, and many later Mu'tazila and the Ash'aris follow him. This shows the permissive trend.

كما ستعرفه وأما صدور الصغائر سهوا فهو جائز اتفاقا بين أكثر أصحابنا وأكثر المعتزلة إلا الصغائر الخسية وهي ما تلحق فاعلها بالأراذل والسفل والحكم عليه بالخسة ودناءه الهمة كسرقة حبة أو القمة فإنها لا تجوز أصلاً لا عمداً ولا سهواً والاتفاق المذكور إنما هو فيما ليس منها كنظرة وكلمة سفه نادرة في خصام وقال الجاحظ : يجوز أن غير صغار الخسة سهواً بشرط أن ينبهوا عليه فينتهوا عنه وقد تبعه فيه يصدر عنهم كثير من المتأخرين من المعتزلة كالنظام والأصم وجعفر بن بشر وبه نقول نحن معاشر الأشاعرة . هذا كله بعد الوحي والاتصاف بالنبوة وأما قبله فقال الجمهور : أي أكثر أصحابنا وجمع من المعتزلة لا يمتنع أن يصدر عنهم كبيرة إذ لا دلالة للمعجزة عليه أي على امتناع الكبيرة قبل البعثة ولا حكم للعقل بامتناعها ولا دلالة سمعية عليه أيضاً وقال أكثر المعتزلة : تمتنع الكبيرة وإن تاب منها لأنه أي الكبيرة يوجب النفرة عمن ارتكبها وهي تمنع عن اتباعه فتفوت مصلحة البعثة ومنهم من منع عما ينفر الطباع عن متابعتهم مطلقاً أي سواء لم يكن ذنباً لهم أو كان كعهر الأمهات إي كونها زانيات والفجور في الآباء ودناءتهم واسترذالهم والصغائر الخسيسة دون غيرها من الصغائر . وقالت الروافض : لا يجوز عليهم صغيرة ولا كبيرة لا عمداً ولا سهواً ولا خطأ في التأويل بل هم مبرؤون عنها قبل الوحي فكيف بعد الوحي.
قوله : (إلا) الحشوية) بفتح الشين منسوبة إلى حشوية على وزن فعولة وهي قرية من قرى خراسان .
قوله : ( يوجب سقوط هيبتهم يرد عليهم أن السقوط في الظهور والصدور وغير مستلزم إياه . اللهم إلا أن يقال : سقوط الهيبة خاصة الكبيرة ولو صدرت سرا .
As for other than disbelief, it is either major sins or minor sins, and each of them is either committed intentionally or unintentionally. So the divisions are four, and each one is either before the mission or after it. As for major sins — i.e., committing them intentionally — the majority of the investigators and imams forbade it, and only the Hashwiyya differed. And most of those who forbid (rely on) its impossibility being derived from revelation. Al-Qadi and the investigators among the Ash'aris said: Infallibility beyond the matter of conveying (the message) is not rationally obligatory, for the miracle does not indicate it. So the impossibility of major sins intentionally is derived from revelation and the consensus of the community before the appearance of the objectors in that. The Mu'tazila said, based on their corrupt principles of rational (determination of) good and evil and the obligation to observe what is beneficial and most beneficial: That is rationally impossible because committing major sins by them intentionally leads to the loss of their awe in hearts and the lowering of their rank in people's eyes, resulting in aversion to them and lack of submission to them, and it entails corrupting creation and abandoning their cultivation, which is contrary to the requirement of reason and wisdom. As for their committing them unintentionally or by mistake in interpretation, the majority permitted it, but the chosen view is contrary. As for minor sins intentionally, the majority permitted them except al-Jubba'i, for he held that a minor sin is not permissible except by way of oversight or mistake in interpretation. This permission from them is only regarding what is not among the lowly minor sins, as you will come to know. As for committing minor sins unintentionally, it is permissible by agreement between most of our companions and most of the Mu'tazila, except the lowly minor sins, which are what place the doer among the lowly and base and pass judgment on him of lowness and meanness of spirit, like stealing a grain or a morsel — these are absolutely impermissible, whether intentionally or unintentionally. The aforementioned agreement is only regarding what is not among them, like a glance or a rare foolish word in an argument. Al-Jahiz said: It is permissible that (sins) other than the lowly minor sins (be committed) unintentionally, provided that they are warned and desist. Many later Mu'tazila followed him, such as al-Nazzam, al-Asamm, and Ja'far ibn Bashshar. And we — the Ash'ari community — say the same. All this is after revelation and the attribution of prophethood. As for before it, the majority — i.e., most of our companions and a group of the Mu'tazila — said: It is not impossible for a major sin to occur from them, for the miracle does not indicate its impossibility before the mission, nor does reason rule its impossibility, nor is there any scriptural evidence for it either. Most of the Mu'tazila said: The major sin is impossible even if he repents from it, because it causes aversion to the one who committed it, and that prevents following him, thus the benefit of the mission is lost. And some of them forbade what repels natural dispositions from following them absolutely — i.e., whether it is a sin for them or not — like the unchastity of mothers (i.e., they are adulteresses), and lasciviousness in fathers, and their baseness and vileness, and the lowly minor sins, not other minor sins. The Rawafid said: No minor or major sin is permissible for them, whether intentionally, unintentionally, or by mistake in interpretation; rather, they are innocent of them before revelation, so how (could they sin) after revelation? His statement: 'except the Hashwiyya' — with a fatha on the shin, attributed to Hashwiyya on the pattern of fa'ula, and it is a village in Khorasan. His statement: 'leads to the loss of their awe' — it is objected against them that the loss in appearance and occurrence does not necessitate it. However, it could be said: The loss of awe is specific to the major sin even if it occurs secretly.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive classification of sins and the positions of various theological groups on whether prophets can commit them. The author begins by dividing sins into major (kaba'ir) and minor (sagha'ir), each either intentional ('amdan) or unintentional (sahw), resulting in four categories, each considered before or after prophethood. For major sins committed intentionally, the majority (Jumhur) of investigators and imams forbid it, with only the Hashwiyya dissenting. The Ash'ari position is that this impossibility is derived from revelation (sam') not reason, as the miracle only guarantees infallibility in conveying the message. The Mu'tazila, based on their rationalist principles, argue it is rationally impossible because it would destroy the prophet's authority. For major sins unintentionally, most permit it but the preferred view opposes. For minor sins intentionally, most permit except al-Jubba'i. For minor sins unintentionally, there is agreement except for 'lowly' (khissiya) sins that degrade the doer, which are absolutely forbidden. Al-Jahiz and others allow non-lowly minor sins unintentionally with warning. The Ash'aris follow this view. Then the author discusses before prophethood: the majority do not consider major sins impossible, while most Mu'tazila do. The Rawafid (Shi'a) hold absolute infallibility even before prophethood. Two marginal notes clarify the term 'Hashwiyya' and discuss the objection that the loss of awe is not necessarily entailed by a secret sin.

Key Terms
سهو
خطأ في التأويل
صغائر الخسة
الجاحظ
الأشاعرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that all minor sins are equally permissible for prophets.
Correction: Lowly minor sins (like stealing a grain) are absolutely prohibited, even unintentionally.

Checkpoint
Which type of sin is absolutely impermissible for prophets according to the passage?
A) Major sins committed intentionally
B) Minor sins committed intentionally
C) Lowly minor sins (صغائر الخسة)
D) Minor sins committed unintentionally

Key Takeaway
Prophets may commit non-lowly minor sins unintentionally according to most scholars, but lowly sins that degrade their status are forbidden.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson teaches that even unintentional lowly sins are absolutely forbidden for prophets because they degrade dignity. Reflect: Are there 'small' sins in your own life—like gossip, a sharp word, or dishonesty in trivial matters—that you excuse as unintentional or harmless? How does the absolute prohibition for prophets challenge you to root out such habits, knowing that your own character matters to Allah?
?
The passage distinguishes between sins committed intentionally and those done by mistake. When you fall into sin, do you honestly examine your intention, or do you quickly classify it as an accident to avoid responsibility? What would change if you held yourself to the same standard of intentionality that this lesson applies to prophets?
?
The lowly minor sins listed (stealing a grain or a morsel) seem insignificant, yet they are absolutely forbidden for prophets. This teaches that even the smallest actions affect one's status. Consider your own daily choices: are there 'grains' or 'morsels'—tiny compromises or careless deeds—that you ignore but that slowly erode your nobility as a believer? What one specific small sin will you commit to eliminate from today?

Prophethood

Sins Before Prophethood and the Rawafid Position
Discussion of sins before prophethood and the Rawafid doctrine of absolute infallibility, plus marginal annotations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differences in opinion regarding sins committed by prophets before their prophetic mission, including the extreme infallibility view of the Rawafid.

Core Idea
Before prophethood, most scholars allow major sins, but the Rawafid absolutely forbid all sins.

The author now shifts to sins occurring before the prophetic mission (قبل البعثة). The majority of Ash'aris and a group of Mu'tazila permit major sins before prophethood, while most Mu'tazila forbid them on rational grounds. The Rawafid (Shi'a) take the most extreme position, asserting complete infallibility from all sins even before prophethood. This lesson also includes a marginal note that critiques the Mu'tazila's argument about loss of awe.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on before prophethood
Note that the majority of Ash'aris and some Mu'tazila do not consider major sins impossible before prophethood, while most Mu'tazila do. Understand the reasoning behind each.
2
Examine the Mu'tazila's additional restriction
Some Mu'tazila forbid not only sins but also actions that repel people, like unchastity of mothers. Identify the examples.
3
Learn the Rawafid position
The Rawafid claim that prophets are innocent of all sins, major and minor, before and after prophethood, including unintentional and mistaken sins.
4
Review the marginal notes
The first note explains the term 'Hashwiyya' (a village in Khorasan). The second note critiques the Mu'tazila argument that intentional major sins cause loss of awe, noting that loss of awe is not necessarily entailed if the sin is secret.

?

The First Proof for Prophetic Infallibility
Sanusi introduces the first proof for prophetic infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that establishes prophetic infallibility from major sins and intentional minor sins.

Core Idea
Prophets cannot sin because it would create a contradiction in the obligation to follow them.

In this passage, Sanusi begins to present the proofs for the Ash'ari position on prophetic infallibility. He first lays down the definition of infallibility (ismah) as protection from major sins absolutely and from minor sins intentionally. Then he gives the first proof: a logical argument that sin would make following the prophet both obligatory and forbidden – an impossibility. Let's examine this argument closely.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the literal translation. Notice the compact style and the conditional structure.
The Arabic includes parentheses that clarify the referent.
2
Identify the conditional argument
The first proof is a conditional sentence: 'if sin occurred from them, following them in what occurred from them would be forbidden.' Recognize this as the core of the proof.
The proof relies on a logical implication.
3
Understand the two premises
The argument has two key premises: (1) sin is forbidden, so following a sinful act is forbidden; (2) following the prophet in all words and deeds is obligatory by consensus and Quran. These are stated in the passage.
The obligation to follow is universal for prophetic actions that are normative.
4
Recognize the contradiction
If a sin occurred, then following that particular action would be both forbidden (because it is sin) and obligatory (because it is part of following the prophet). This contradiction is impossible, so sin cannot occur.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
5
Connect to broader doctrine
This proof establishes that prophets are infallible from major sins and intentional minor sins. The same logic applies to all their actions and words.
The passage mentions this is the first of eight proofs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(لنا على ما هو المختار عندنا وهو أن الأنبياء في زمان نبوتهم معصومون عن الكبائر مطلقاً وعن الصغائر عمداً ( وجوه : الأول : لو صدر منهم الذنب لحرم اتباعهم فيما صدر عنهم ضرورة أنه يحرم ارتكاب الذنب ) وأنه ( أي اتباعهم ( ) في أقوالهم وأفعالهم ) واجب للإجماع عليه . ( ولقوله تعالى : قل إن كنتم تحبون الله فاتبعوني يحببكم الله ﴾ [آل عمران : ۳۱ ]
(We have, according to what is chosen with us – that the prophets during the time of their prophethood are infallible from major sins absolutely and from minor sins intentionally – proofs: The first: if sin occurred from them, following them in what occurred from them would be forbidden, of necessity because committing sin is forbidden. And that following them in their words and actions is obligatory by consensus. And by His statement Almighty: 'Say: If you love Allah, follow me, Allah will love you' [Al-Imran:31].)
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage begins the presentation of proofs for the Ash'ari position that prophets are infallible from all major sins and from intentional minor sins during their prophethood. It introduces that there are several proofs (wujuh). The first proof is a logical argument: If a prophet committed a sin, then following that prophet in that particular action would be forbidden, because the action itself is sinful and thus prohibited. However, following the prophet in all his words and deeds is obligatory by consensus, as indicated by the Qur'anic verse 'Follow me, Allah will love you.' Therefore, if sin occurred, it would create a contradiction: it would be both obligatory and forbidden to follow that action. Hence, sin cannot occur.

Key Terms
معصوم
كبيرة
صغيرة
عمد
اتباع
إجماع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof claims that every single action of a prophet is obligatory to follow.
Correction: The obligation to follow the prophet applies to his normative teachings and actions that are part of the Shari'a, not to every incidental action. The proof uses the general principle that the prophet's actions are to be emulated in matters of religion.

Checkpoint
What is the conclusion of the first proof?
A) Prophets must not sin because sinning is forbidden
B) If prophets sinned, following them would be both obligatory and forbidden
C) Prophets cannot sin because they are loved by Allah
D) Following prophets is not obligatory

Key Takeaway
The first proof for prophetic infallibility is a logical argument that any sin would lead to a contradiction in the obligation to follow the prophet, so sin cannot occur.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof shows that following the prophet is obligatory without exception. Is there any area of your life where you have made an exception, thinking that your own judgment supersedes his command? What would it cost you to submit fully?
?
If you truly believed that any sin from the prophet is impossible, how would that change the way you approach his sunnah? Would you still cherry-pick easy parts and ignore challenging commands like the one about lowering your gaze or giving in charity?
?
You claim to love Allah by loving His prophet. But this proof demands consistency: your love must translate into obedience in every detail. Which habit or relationship in your life right now directly contradicts the prophet's teachings? Will you abandon it today?

Second Proof: Rejection of a Sinner's Testimony
Sanusi gives the second proof: if prophets sinned, their testimony would be rejected.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second kalam proof for prophetic infallibility: the argument from the rejection of a sinner's testimony.

Core Idea
A prophet's message is testimony; sin would make it unreliable.

Sanusi now presents the second rational proof for 'ismah (infallibility). It draws on the undeniable principle that a sinner's testimony is rejected in both worldly and religious matters. If prophets could sin, their entire prophetic mission would be undermined. This lesson unpacks the logical structure of that argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Notice the logical flow: condition, evidence, conclusion.
The passage is terse; each clause carries weight.
2
Identify the conditional statement
The proof begins with 'if they sinned' (لو أذنبوا). Identify the necessary consequence that follows and the two pieces of evidence supporting it.
3
Examine the evidence: consensus and Qur'an
The passage cites consensus (الإجماع) and the Qur'anic verse (49:6) as proof that a sinner's testimony is rejected. Reflect on why both are considered authoritative.
Consensus here refers to scholarly agreement on the legal principle.
4
Consider the rhetorical conclusion
The passage ends with a rhetorical question contrasting worldly goods with the eternal religion. Understand how this reinforces the point that prophetic testimony cannot be rejected.
The 'little that quickly perishes' refers to material wealth.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني لو أذنبوا لردت شهادتهم إذ لا شهادة لفاسق بالإجماع ولقوله تعالى : إن جاءكم فاسق بنبأ فتبينوا ﴾ [ الحجرات : ٦] ، واللازم باطل بالإجماع ولأن من لا تقبل شهادته في القليل) الزائل بسرعة ( من متاع الدنيا كيف تسمع شهادته في الدين القيم ) أي القائم (إلى يوم القيامة ؟
The second: if they sinned, their testimony would be rejected, because there is no testimony for a sinner by consensus, and by His statement Almighty: 'If a sinner comes to you with news, verify it' [al-Hujurat:6]. And the necessary consequence is false by consensus, and because whoever's testimony is not accepted in the little that quickly perishes from the goods of this world, how can his testimony be heard in the enduring religion until the Day of Resurrection?
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage presents the second proof for prophetic infallibility. It argues that if prophets committed sins, they would be considered sinners (fasiq). By consensus, the testimony of a sinner is not accepted, and the Qur'an (49:6) commands verifying news brought by a sinner. Therefore, if prophets sinned, their testimony (which includes their prophetic message) would be rejected. But it is unacceptable that the testimony of prophets in matters of religion be rejected, especially since even in worldly matters their testimony would be deemed unreliable. Thus, prophets must be sinless.

Key Terms
شهادة
فاسق
تبيين
إجماع

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof implies that prophets are only witnesses in legal court cases.
Correction: The proof uses 'testimony' (شهادة) broadly to refer to their entire prophetic mission; sin would undermine their credibility in conveying revelation.

Checkpoint
What does the second proof argue would happen if prophets sinned?
A) They would lose their prophethood
B) Their testimony and message would be rejected
C) They would be punished by stoning
D) They would be forgiven immediately

Key Takeaway
The second proof shows that the very nature of prophethood requires sinlessness, because sin would nullify the trustworthiness of their message.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
If you would not accept a sinner's word about a small worldly matter, how can you justify neglecting the Prophet's testimony about the greatest matter—your eternal salvation? What step will you take today to treat his message with the weight it deserves?

Third Proof: Forbidding Rebuke of Prophets
Sanusi presents the third proof: sin would require rebuke, but rebuking prophets is forbidden.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third proof for prophetic infallibility: that a prophet's sin would create a contradiction between the obligation to rebuke and the prohibition of harming prophets, and would entail impossible divine threats.

Core Idea
A prophet's sin would necessitate forbidden rebuke and impossible punishments.

Sanusi now presents the third argument for 'isma (infallibility). This proof uses the obligation to enjoin good and forbid evil, which would require rebuking a sinful prophet. But rebuking a prophet is a form of harm, which is utterly forbidden. Moreover, sin would imply Qur'anic punishments that cannot apply to Allah's chosen messengers. Let us examine this tightly reasoned proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the literal translation. Let the structure of the argument become clear before analyzing.
Notice the use of conditional language: 'if a sin occurred'.
2
Identify the two main premises
The proof rests on two pillars: (1) sin obligates rebuke due to commanding good and forbidding evil, (2) rebuking a prophet is harming, and harming is forbidden. Trace how these lead to a contradiction.
3
Examine the additional Qur'anic evidence
Sanusi cites several verses that would apply if prophets sinned: hellfire, curse, blame. Understand that these are impossible for prophets by consensus.
The verses are from al-Ahzab, al-Jinn, Hud, al-Saff, and al-Baqarah.
4
Understand the conclusion
Since rebuke is both obligatory and forbidden, and the divine threats are false, sin cannot occur. This proves prophetic infallibility.
The proof is apagogic (reductio ad absurdum).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : إن صدر عنه) ذنب (وجب زجرهم) وتعنيفهم لعموم وجوب الأمر بالمعروف والنهي عن المنكر ولا شك أن زجرهم إيذاء لهم ) وإيذاؤهم حرام إجماعاً ولقوله ) تعالى : ( والذين يؤذون الله ورسوله ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٥٧] ، الآية و أيضاً لو أذنبوا لدخلوا تحت ) قوله ومن يعص الله ورسوله فإن له نار جهنم له [الجن: ٢٣] و ) تحت (قوله : ألا لعنة الله على الظالمين ﴾ [هود : ۱۸] و) تحت (قوله: لوماً كأحد من من У = ومذمة ولم تقولون ما لا تفعلون ﴾ [الصف : ٢] وقوله : ( أتأمرون الناس بالبر وتنسون أنفسكم ﴾ [البقرة : ٤٤])، فيلزم كونهم موعودين بعذاب جهنم وملعونين ومذمومين وكل ذلك باطل إجماعاً .
The third: if a sin occurred from him, rebuking and reprimanding them would be obligatory due to the generality of the obligation of commanding good and forbidding evil. And there is no doubt that rebuking them is harming them, and harming them is forbidden by consensus, and by His statement Almighty: 'Those who harm Allah and His Messenger' [al-Ahzab:57]. And also if they sinned, they would fall under His statement: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, indeed for him is the fire of Hell' [al-Jinn:23], and under His statement: 'Indeed, the curse of Allah is upon the wrongdoers' [Hud:18], and under His statement: 'blame, like one of ... and blame, and why do you say what you do not do?' [al-Saff:2], and His statement: 'Do you enjoin righteousness upon others and forget yourselves?' [al-Baqarah:44]. Thus they would be promised the fire of Hell, cursed, and blamed, and all that is false by consensus.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof for prophetic infallibility. It argues that if a prophet committed a sin, it would be obligatory to rebuke and reprimand him because of the general obligation to enjoin good and forbid evil. But rebuking a prophet constitutes harming him, and harming prophets is forbidden by consensus and by the Qur'anic verse (33:57). Additionally, if prophets sinned, they would fall under various Qur'anic threats such as being subject to hellfire (72:23), being cursed (11:18), being blamed (61:2), and being told off for hypocrisy (2:44). Since these consequences are false for prophets by consensus, sin cannot occur. The proof concludes that all such consequences are invalid, establishing infallibility.

Key Terms
زجر
إيذاء
أمر بالمعروف
نهي عن المنكر
لعن
تبعات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think this proof is about any harm to prophets, but it is specifically about rebuke that would be obligatory due to sin.
Correction: The proof hinges on the obligation to rebuke a sinner, not on general harm. Rebuke is harm, so it becomes forbidden, creating a contradiction.

Checkpoint
Why would a prophet's sin obligate rebuke that is forbidden?
A) Because rebuke is always bad
B) Because rebuke would harm the prophet, which is forbidden
C) Because prophets are not subject to rebuke
D) Because rebuke is not obligatory for sins

Key Takeaway
The third proof shows that prophetic sin is impossible because it would necessitate both an obligatory rebuke that is forbidden and divine punishments that cannot apply to prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If rebuking a prophet for sin would be both obligatory and forbidden, what does that contradiction reveal about the absolute perfection Allah demands from His messengers? How does this reshape your expectation of human leadership?
?
The proof argues that sin would necessarily bring blame and punishment. In your own life, when you sin, do you truly feel the weight of divine blame and the threat of punishment—or have you become desensitized? What would it take for you to take that threat as seriously as this proof demands?
?
This lesson shows that harming prophets is forbidden. In your heart, do you harbor any resentment or disrespect toward the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) because of trials in your life? How can you actively purge that from your soul starting today?

Fourth Proof: Multiplied Punishment
Sanusi gives the fourth proof: prophets would deserve multiplied punishment if they sinned.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the possibility of prophets sinning would lead to multiplied punishment, making it incompatible with divine wisdom.

Core Idea
Greater honor brings greater responsibility — and greater punishment for sin.

Sanusi presents the fourth proof for prophetic impeccability: if prophets could sin, they would deserve multiplied punishment due to their elevated rank. This argument draws on the principle that the greater the favor received, the more severe the consequence for opposing it with disobedience. The proof is supported by a Qur'anic example and logical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: a conditional statement, a general principle, a scriptural example, and a conclusion.
The passage is concise, so read it twice.
2
Identify the core reasoning
The author argues that the greater the honor (rank), the more severe the punishment for sin. This is based on both reason and transmitted texts. Find the phrase 'لكل رتبة في الكرامة يستحق أشد العذاب'.
This is the key logical link.
3
Reflect on the example and conclusion
Consider the verse about the Prophet's wives (33:30) and how it illustrates the principle. Then see how Sanusi applies it to prophethood itself, showing that any sin would lead to immense punishment, which is contrary to divine mercy.
This shows why sin is impossible for prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع : ولكانوا على تقدير صدور الذنب عنهم ( أسوء حالاً من عصاة الأمة إذ يضاعف لهم ) أي للأنبياء (العذاب ) على الذنب إذ لا على رتبة في الكرامة ( يستحق ) عقلا ونقلا ( أشد العذاب لمقابلته أعظم النعم ) المفاضة عليه ) بالمعصية ولذلك ضوعف حد الحر وقيل : يا نساء النبي لستن النساء من يأت منكن بفاحشة مبينة يضاعف لها العذاب ﴾ [الأحزاب : ۳۰] ومن المعلوم أن النبوة أجل من كل نعمة فمن قابلها بالمعصية استحق العذاب أضعافاً مضاعفة .
The fourth: and they would be, on the supposition of sin occurring from them, in a worse state than the sinners of the community, because the punishment is multiplied for them - meaning the prophets - for the sin, since for every rank in honor, there is deserved, rationally and by transmission, a severer punishment for opposing it with sin due to the greatest favors conferred upon them. For this reason, the punishment of the free man was doubled, and it was said: 'O wives of the Prophet, you are not like other women. Whoever among you commits a manifest immorality, the punishment will be doubled for her' [al-Ahzab:30]. And it is known that prophethood is greater than every favor, so whoever opposes it with sin deserves doubled punishment.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth proof. It argues that if prophets sinned, they would be in an even worse state than ordinary sinners because their punishment would be multiplied. This is because the greater the honor and favors one has received, the more severe the punishment for sinning against those favors. The text gives the example of the wives of the Prophet (33:30) whose punishment is doubled due to their special status. Since prophethood is the greatest favor, any sin by a prophet would deserve immense punishment. Therefore, it would be unreasonable and contrary to divine wisdom for prophets to sin, as that would subject them to extreme punishment.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The multiplication of punishment is arbitrary or purely punitive.
Correction: The multiplication is based on the principle that greater honor brings greater responsibility; it is a rational and revealed consequence of rank.

Key Takeaway

Fifth Proof: Sinners Cannot Attain God's Covenant
Sanusi gives the fifth proof: sinners cannot attain God's covenant, but prophets have the covenant of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the fifth proof uses the Qur'anic principle that God's covenant excludes wrongdoers, and the a fortiori argument that establishes the necessity of sinlessness for prophets.

Core Idea
If God’s covenant excludes wrongdoers, then prophets, who hold the highest covenant, must be sinless.

Sanusi now presents a proof rooted in a clear Qur'anic declaration: God's covenant does not reach the wrongdoers. Since prophets are the recipients of the greatest covenant—prophethood or even imamate—they must be sinless. This lesson unpacks the verse and the logical argument built upon it.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage
Read the Arabic text and its literal translation carefully. Notice the citation of Quran 2:124 and the two possible interpretations of 'covenant'.
Pay attention to the phrase 'بطريق الأولى' (a fortiori).
2
Understand the verse's application
The verse states that wrongdoers (zalimun) are excluded from God's covenant. A sinner is a wrongdoer to himself, so he cannot receive any covenant from Allah.
3
Analyze the a fortiori argument
Sanusi offers two interpretations: if 'covenant' means prophethood, the conclusion is direct; if it means imamate, then by a fortiori reasoning, one who does not deserve the lesser (imamate) certainly does not deserve the greater (prophethood).
This shows the flexibility and strength of the proof.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The proof establishes that prophets must be sinless (ma'sum) because they hold the highest covenant from Allah, which cannot be given to wrongdoers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس : ولم ينالوا أيضاً ( عهده تعالى لقوله : لا ينال عهدي الظالمين ) [ البقرة : ١٢٤ ] ، والمذنب ظالم لنفسه ) وأي عهد أعظم من النبوة ) فإن حمل مافي الآية على عهده النبوة فذاك وإن حمل على عهد الإمامة فبطريق الأولى لأن يستحق الأدنى لا يستحق الأعلى .
The fifth: and they would not attain His covenant, due to His statement: 'My covenant does not include the wrongdoers' [al-Baqarah:124]. And a sinner is a wrongdoer to himself. And what covenant is greater than prophethood? So if what is in the verse is interpreted as the covenant of prophethood, that is it; and if interpreted as the covenant of imamate, then by a fortiori reasoning, because the one who does not deserve the lower does not deserve the higher.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth proof. It cites the Qur'anic verse (2:124) where God says His covenant does not include the wrongdoers (zalimun). A sinner is a wrongdoer to himself. The 'covenant' here is interpreted as prophethood or imamate. If it means prophethood, then directly, a sinner cannot be a prophet. If it means imamate (leadership), then by a fortiori reasoning, if one does not deserve the lesser covenant (imamate), then he certainly does not deserve the greater one (prophethood). Therefore, prophets must be sinless to receive God's covenant.

Key Terms
عهد
ظالم
نبوة
إمامة
بطريق الأولى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof only works if 'covenant' is interpreted as prophethood.
Correction: Even if 'covenant' is interpreted as imamate, the a fortiori argument still proves that sinners cannot be prophets.

Checkpoint

B) If a sinner can be a prophet, he can be an imam
C) Prophethood is lesser than imamate
D) Wrongdoers can receive the covenant

Key Takeaway
The fifth proof uses the Qur'anic principle that God's covenant excludes wrongdoers, and applies it a fortiori to establish the necessity of prophets' sinlessness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's covenant excludes wrongdoers, what does that mean for your own relationship with God when you sin? How does this truth challenge your complacency about minor sins?
?
The greatest covenant belongs to prophets, but you too are called to enter God's covenant through faith. Are there sins you are holding onto that you know exclude you from the full experience of that covenant?
?
Sanusi argues that a sinner does not even deserve imamate, let alone prophethood. How does this shape your understanding of the seriousness of sin and the need for constant repentance?

The Sixth Proof: Sincerity and Sinlessness
Sanusi presents the sixth proof and includes its refutation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the sixth proof for prophetic sinlessness based on sincerity and its scholarly refutation.

Core Idea
Satan cannot tempt the sincere; prophets are sincere, so they cannot sin.

The sixth proof argues that sin arises from Satan's temptation, but Satan cannot tempt the sincere. Since the Qur'an declares prophets like Abraham, Isaac, Jacob, and Joseph as sincere, they must be sinless. However, a refutation is noted: the verses do not explicitly exclude other prophets from being tempted. This lesson unpacks the argument and its limitations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note how the argument is structured: a conditional statement, a proof from the Qur'an, and a refutation.
The refutation is part of the text, not an addition.
2
Identify the core logical structure
Break down the argument into premise, evidence, and refutation. The premise: sin comes from Satan's temptation. The evidence: Satan cannot tempt the sincere. The refutation: the verses only mention some prophets, not all.
3
Reflect on the refutation
Consider why the author includes a refutation he does not accept. Think about how later proofs may strengthen the case.
This shows scholarly honesty.
4
Connect to the larger theme
Recall that prophetic sinlessness is a central claim. See how this proof contributes but is not conclusive alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس : (ولكانوا أيضاً غير مخلصين لأن الذنب بإغواء الشيطان وهو لا يغوي المخلصين لقوله تعالى : ( حكاية عنه على سبيل التصديق ( لاغوينوهم أجمعين إلا عبادك منهم المخلصين ﴾ [الحجر: ٣٩]، واللازم باطل لقوله تعالى : في حق إبراهيم وإسحاق ويعقوب و إنا أخلصناهم بخالصة ذكرى الدار [ ص : ٤٦] ، وفي حق (يوسف إنه من عبادنا المخلصين)، وقد رد على هذا بأنه لا يدل على أن غير هؤلاء لم يصل إليهم إغواء إبليس ولم يذنبوا . السابع : قوله تعالى : ولقد صدق عليهم إبليس ظنه فاتبعوه إلا فريقاً من المؤمنين له سبأ : ٢٠ ] ، فالذين لم يتبعوه إن كانوا هم الأنبياء فذاك مطلوبنا، ( وإلا ) أي وإن لم يكونوا إياهم بل كانوا غيرهم ( فالأنبياء ) أيضاً لم يتبعوه ( بالطريق الأولى) فإنهم بذلك أحرى من سائر المؤمنين ( أو تقول : لو كان ذلك الفريق غير الأنبياء لكانوا أفضل من الأنبياء لقوله تعالى إن أكرمكم عند الله أتقاكم ﴾ [الحجرات : ١٣ ] ، وتفضيل غير الأنبياء عليهم باطل بالإجماع فوجب القطع بأن الأنبياء لم يتبعوه ولم يذنبوه. ( الثامن : أنه تعالى قسم المكلفين إلى حزب الله وحزب الشيطان فلو أذنبوا قوله : (إنا أخلصناهم بخالصة ذكرى الدار أي جعلناهم خالصين لنا بخصلة خالصة لا شوب فيها، هي ذكرى الدار أي ذكرهم للآخرة دائماً، فإن خلوصهم في الطاعة بسببها .
The sixth: and they would also not be sincere, because sin is by the temptation of Satan, and he does not tempt the sincere ones, due to His statement (narrating from him, by way of confirmation): 'I will surely mislead them all, except Your sincere servants among them' [al-Hijr:39]. And the necessary consequence is false, due to His statement regarding Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob: 'Indeed, We purified them with a pure quality: the remembrance of the home' [Sad:46], and regarding Joseph: 'Indeed, he is among Our sincere servants.' And it has been refuted that this does not indicate that others besides these did not receive the temptation of Iblis and did not sin. The seventh: His statement Almighty: 'And Iblis had already confirmed his assumption concerning them, so they followed him, except a party of the believers' [Saba:20]. If those who did not follow him are the prophets, that is what we seek. Otherwise, (i.e., if they are not them but others), then the prophets also did not follow him, by a fortiori reasoning, because they are more worthy of that than other believers. Or you could say: if that party was other than the prophets, they would be better than the prophets, due to His statement: 'Indeed, the most noble of you to Allah is the most righteous' [al-Hujurat:13]. And preferring non-prophets over them is false by consensus, so it is necessary to conclude that the prophets did not follow him and did not sin. The eighth: that He Almighty divided the obligated ones into the party of Allah and the party of Satan, so if they sinned... His statement: 'Indeed, We purified them with a pure quality: the remembrance of the home' meaning: We made them pure for Ourselves with a pure quality with no admixture, which is the remembrance of the home, i.e., their constant remembrance of the Hereafter, for their purity in obedience is due to it.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage presents three related proofs. The sixth proof argues that sin would indicate lack of sincerity (ikhlas), because Satan tempts all except the sincere. But the Qur'an declares prophets like Abraham, Isaac, Jacob, and Joseph as sincere. However, the text notes a refutation: that verse does not prove that other prophets were not tempted. The seventh proof uses the verse about Iblis confirming his assumption that most people would follow him, except a party. If that party is the prophets, that is the point. If not, then prophets are even more likely to be among that party, or if that party is more pious than prophets, that would be impossible by consensus. The eighth proof (incomplete) states that Allah divided people into two parties (God's and Satan's); if prophets sinned, they would belong to Satan's party, which is false. The footnote explains a phrase from the sixth proof about 'ikhlas' in relation to the verse about Sad.

Key Terms
مخلص
إغواء
إبليس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The sixth proof is decisive and unassailable.
Correction: The author himself includes a refutation, showing that the proof is not conclusive on its own but is supported by other arguments.

Checkpoint
What is the main Qur'anic verse used as evidence in the sixth proof?
A) Surah al-Hijr verse 39
B) Surah Sad verse 46
C) Surah Yusuf verse 36
D) Both A and B

Key Takeaway
The sixth proof uses sincerity as a basis for sinlessness but acknowledges a valid critique, showing the need for multiple proofs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This passage describes the sincere as those whom Satan cannot tempt. Look honestly at your own life: where have you been defeated by temptation? Does that reveal a lack of sincerity? What single change in your heart will you ask Allah for today to become more sincere?
?
The proof from sincerity is limited to those prophets explicitly called sincere in the Quran. You are not a prophet, but you can strive for sincerity. If you were to die tonight, would you be counted among the sincere? What habit are you clinging to that proves otherwise?
?
The refutation shows that one proof alone is insufficient for certainty. In your own faith, are you relying on a single piece of evidence for a core belief, like the sinlessness of prophets? What other proofs or evidences have you personally examined? Commit to studying one additional proof this week.
