The Seventh Proof: Following Satan and Prophetic Priority
Sanusi presents the seventh proof using Saba 20 and a fortiori reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seventh proof for prophetic sinlessness, which uses the Qur'anic verse about Iblis's assumption and a fortiori reasoning.

Core Idea
Prophets are more likely than other believers to resist Satan, so they must be sinless.

The seventh proof is based on Surah Saba verse 20, where Iblis's assumption that most people would follow him is confirmed, except a party of believers. The proof argues that either that party includes the prophets (which proves sinlessness) or it does not; in the latter case, the prophets would be even more deserving to be among that party, or else non-prophets would be better, which is false by consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Focus on the logical structure: a conditional argument with two branches, both leading to the conclusion that prophets did not follow Satan.
Note the use of 'a fortiori' (بالطريق الأولى).
2
Identify the two branches
First branch: the 'party of believers' are the prophets. Second branch: if not, then prophets are more worthy to be that party, or else non-prophets would be better than prophets.
3
Understand the a fortiori argument
The phrase 'بالطريق الأولى' indicates that if other believers can resist Satan, prophets certainly can. This is a common kalam reasoning.
4
Reflect on the consensus
The argument uses the consensus that non-prophets cannot be better than prophets. This consensus supports the conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادس : (ولكانوا أيضاً غير مخلصين لأن الذنب بإغواء الشيطان وهو لا يغوي المخلصين لقوله تعالى : ( حكاية عنه على سبيل التصديق ( لاغوينوهم أجمعين إلا عبادك منهم المخلصين ﴾ [الحجر: ٣٩]، واللازم باطل لقوله تعالى : في حق إبراهيم وإسحاق ويعقوب و إنا أخلصناهم بخالصة ذكرى الدار [ ص : ٤٦] ، وفي حق (يوسف إنه من عبادنا المخلصين)، وقد رد على هذا بأنه لا يدل على أن غير هؤلاء لم يصل إليهم إغواء إبليس ولم يذنبوا . السابع : قوله تعالى : ولقد صدق عليهم إبليس ظنه فاتبعوه إلا فريقاً من المؤمنين له سبأ : ٢٠ ] ، فالذين لم يتبعوه إن كانوا هم الأنبياء فذاك مطلوبنا، ( وإلا ) أي وإن لم يكونوا إياهم بل كانوا غيرهم ( فالأنبياء ) أيضاً لم يتبعوه ( بالطريق الأولى) فإنهم بذلك أحرى من سائر المؤمنين ( أو تقول : لو كان ذلك الفريق غير الأنبياء لكانوا أفضل من الأنبياء لقوله تعالى إن أكرمكم عند الله أتقاكم ﴾ [الحجرات : ١٣ ] ، وتفضيل غير الأنبياء عليهم باطل بالإجماع فوجب القطع بأن الأنبياء لم يتبعوه ولم يذنبوه. ( الثامن : أنه تعالى قسم المكلفين إلى حزب الله وحزب الشيطان فلو أذنبوا قوله : (إنا أخلصناهم بخالصة ذكرى الدار أي جعلناهم خالصين لنا بخصلة خالصة لا شوب فيها، هي ذكرى الدار أي ذكرهم للآخرة دائماً، فإن خلوصهم في الطاعة بسببها .
The sixth: and they would also not be sincere, because sin is by the temptation of Satan, and he does not tempt the sincere ones, due to His statement (narrating from him, by way of confirmation): 'I will surely mislead them all, except Your sincere servants among them' [al-Hijr:39]. And the necessary consequence is false, due to His statement regarding Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob: 'Indeed, We purified them with a pure quality: the remembrance of the home' [Sad:46], and regarding Joseph: 'Indeed, he is among Our sincere servants.' And it has been refuted that this does not indicate that others besides these did not receive the temptation of Iblis and did not sin. The seventh: His statement Almighty: 'And Iblis had already confirmed his assumption concerning them, so they followed him, except a party of the believers' [Saba:20]. If those who did not follow him are the prophets, that is what we seek. Otherwise, (i.e., if they are not them but others), then the prophets also did not follow him, by a fortiori reasoning, because they are more worthy of that than other believers. Or you could say: if that party was other than the prophets, they would be better than the prophets, due to His statement: 'Indeed, the most noble of you to Allah is the most righteous' [al-Hujurat:13]. And preferring non-prophets over them is false by consensus, so it is necessary to conclude that the prophets did not follow him and did not sin. The eighth: that He Almighty divided the obligated ones into the party of Allah and the party of Satan, so if they sinned... His statement: 'Indeed, We purified them with a pure quality: the remembrance of the home' meaning: We made them pure for Ourselves with a pure quality with no admixture, which is the remembrance of the home, i.e., their constant remembrance of the Hereafter, for their purity in obedience is due to it.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage presents three related proofs. The sixth proof argues that sin would indicate lack of sincerity (ikhlas), because Satan tempts all except the sincere. But the Qur'an declares prophets like Abraham, Isaac, Jacob, and Joseph as sincere. However, the text notes a refutation: that verse does not prove that other prophets were not tempted. The seventh proof uses the verse about Iblis confirming his assumption that most people would follow him, except a party. If that party is the prophets, that is the point. If not, then prophets are even more likely to be among that party, or if that party is more pious than prophets, that would be impossible by consensus. The eighth proof (incomplete) states that Allah divided people into two parties (God's and Satan's); if prophets sinned, they would belong to Satan's party, which is false. The footnote explains a phrase from the sixth proof about 'ikhlas' in relation to the verse about Sad.

حزب الله
حزب الشيطان
إبليس

Checkpoint
What is the main Qur'anic verse used in the seventh proof?
A) Surah al-Hijr verse 39
B) Surah Saba verse 20
C) Surah al-Hujurat verse 13
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
The seventh proof uses logical branching and consensus to show that prophets must be among those who resisted Satan.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Iblis assumed that most people would follow him, and the Quran confirms his assumption. Which side of that assumption does your daily life place you on? What specific habits or choices prove that you are part of the 'party that did not follow'?
?
If you claim to be among the believers who resist Satan, what evidence from your obedience to divine commands and avoidance of sin can you point to today? Would your actions convince an observer that you are truly following Allah and not Iblis?
?
The a fortiori argument shows that prophets are even more worthy than other believers to resist sin. How does the example of the prophets challenge you to raise your standard of righteousness, especially in areas where you compromise?

The Eighth Proof: Allah's Division into Two Parties
Sanusi begins the eighth proof but it is cut off.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the incomplete eighth proof, which argues that prophets cannot sin because they belong to the party of Allah, not the party of Satan.

Core Idea
Allah divides people into His party and Satan's party; prophets cannot be in Satan's party.

The eighth proof is fragmentary but its core is clear: Allah has divided the obligated people into two parties—the party of Allah and the party of Satan. If prophets sinned, they would belong to Satan's party, which is impossible. The proof is incomplete in the text, but the reasoning is straightforward.

Guided Path
1
Read the available passage
The Arabic cuts off after 'فلو أذنبوا' (so if they sinned). Understand that the implied conclusion is that they would then belong to Satan's party.
The text likely continued with 'لكانوا من حزب الشيطان' or similar.
2
Reconstruct the full argument
Based on the context, the argument is: Allah divided people into two parties (Saba 20-21). Prophets must be in Allah's party. If they sinned, they would be in Satan's party, which is false.
3
Connect to the footnote
The footnote about 'إنا أخلصناهم' explains a phrase from the sixth proof, not the eighth. It is separate.
4
Evaluate the proof's strength
Even though the proof is incomplete, it relies on the clear Qur'anic division and the assumption that prophets are inherently part of Allah's party.

Opponent's Objection and Rebuttal on Prophetic Infallibility
The author presents three rebuttals to the opponent's claim that prophets can sin forgetfully.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the opponent's argument that prophets could sin forgetfully and the author's multi-pronged rebuttal demonstrating that such sins are incompatible with prophethood.

Core Idea
Even forgetful sins would destroy trust in prophethood.

In this passage, the author engages with an opponent who claims that prophets could commit major sins forgetfully after their mission. This objection challenges the doctrine of prophetic infallibility. The author responds with three distinct arguments, each dismantling a different basis for the opponent's claim.

Guided Path
1
Read the opponent's objection
Identify the claim that prophets can sin forgetfully and intentionally after their mission.
The opponent is described as one who permits major sins out of forgetfulness.
2
Understand the first two rebuttals
Note how the author reinterprets the opponent's proof texts: 'party of Satan' means disbelievers, and the proof does not apply to all prophets.
The author challenges both the scope and the generality of the proofs.
3
Examine the third rebuttal
See the practical problem: if prophets could forget, followers would be obliged to follow false rulings, which is absurd.
The author hints at a requirement that prophets immediately correct themselves.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج المخالف ( الذاهب إلى جواز صدور الكبائر عنهم بعد البعثة سهوا وجواز
عمداً
ومع
قوله : ( فلو أذنبوا لكانوا من حزب الشيطان فيه أن حزب الشيطان الكافر كما يدل عليه
سياق الآيات في آخر سورة المجادلة، ولو سلم العموم فهو المذنب الغير التائب أو العامد . قوله : ( التاسع إلخ ) فيه أنه لا عموم له لجميع الأنبياء ولو سلم فلا ينفي السهو على أن
صحة الاستثناء في استعمال ما لا يستلزم صحته في هذا الاستعمال. قوله : ( فإن الاتباع إنما يجب إلخ قيل عليه : لا يخفى أن المخاطب إنما يأخذ الحكم من المبلغ وأمر السهو والنسيان وفلتات ،اللسان ليس مما يعرفه المخاطب أنه كذلك حتى يجتنب عن الاتباع وهو مأمور بالاتباع، فلو جوز ذلك لزم جواز الاتباع بل وجوبه في الأحكام الكاذبة اللهم إلا أن يشترط تنبه الأنبياء في الحال وتنبيههم للمخاطبين فتأمل .
And the opponent argued—the one who goes to the permissibility of major sins from them after the mission forgetfully and permissibility intentionally—and with [؟]. His saying: (For if they sinned, they would be from the party of Satan) has in it that the party of Satan is the disbeliever, as indicated by the context of the verses at the end of Surat al-Mujadila; and if the generality is granted, it refers to the unrepentant sinner or the intentional one. His saying: (the ninth, etc.) has in it that there is no generality for all prophets; and if granted, it does not negate forgetfulness, given that the validity of exception in usage does not necessitate its validity in this usage. His saying: (for following is only obligatory, etc.) it was objected to him: it is not hidden that the addressee only takes the ruling from the conveyer; and the matter of forgetfulness, forgetfulness, and slips of the tongue is not something the addressee knows to be the case so that he refrains from following, while he is commanded to follow. So if that is permitted, it would necessitate the permissibility, rather obligation, of following in false rulings, unless it is stipulated that the prophets become aware instantly and alert the addressees. So ponder.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage begins with the opponent's objection: those who allow prophets to commit major sins forgetfully after their mission, and also intentionally (possibly a fragment). Then three notes are presented. The first note addresses the eighth proof (about the party of Satan): the opponent argues that 'party of Satan' refers to disbelievers, not all sinners; even if general, it applies only to unrepentant or intentional sinners. The second note addresses the ninth proof: it argues that there is no generality covering all prophets, and even if there were, it does not negate forgetfulness; also the validity of exception in linguistic usage does not guarantee its validity in this context. The third note addresses the author's earlier statement that following is only obligatory for intentional actions; the opponent objects that the common person does not know whether the prophet is forgetful or not, so if forgetfulness were possible, the common person would be obliged to follow even false rulings, which is absurd—unless the prophet immediately realizes and corrects himself. The author concludes with 'ponder', suggesting this is a strong rebuttal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The opponent believes that the Quranic proofs against prophets sinning only apply to intentional sins or are not absolute.
Correction: The author shows that even forgetful sins are covered because they would undermine trust and lead followers into error.

Checkpoint

D) The proof relies on a false interpretation.

Key Takeaway
The doctrine of prophetic infallibility is comprehensive, covering even forgetful sins because any sin would erode the trust essential to prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The rebuttal argues that even a forgetful sin from a prophet would destroy trust and make following impossible. Examine your own heart: In what areas of your life do you treat the Prophet’s teachings with less certainty than you treat the words of a trusted friend? What would change if you truly believed that every command from him is absolutely correct, free from even forgetful error? Will you begin today to act on that belief, even in the most difficult command?
?
The author says 'ponder' at the end of the rebuttal. Stop and think: Are there any prophetic teachings you have dismissed or neglected because of your own 'forgetfulness' or by excusing yourself as 'only human'? Could it be that your forgetfulness is actually a lack of care? What is one forgotten sunnah you will recommit to this week, not as an option but as an obligation?
?
If the very possibility of a prophet slipping forgetfully would obligate us to follow false rulings, then how can we ever justify our own selective obedience? What is one area where you have knowingly not followed the prophetic guidance, and what excuse have you used? Is that excuse more valid than the excuses the opponent gave? How will you remove that barrier today?

Objector's Argument and General Answer
Sanusi states the objector's argument and the initial general answer regarding solitary and mutawatir reports.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objector's use of prophetic stories and the principle that solitary reports are rejected while mutawatir reports are interpreted to preserve infallibility.

Core Idea
Solitary reports cannot outweigh prophetic infallibility; mutawatir reports require careful interpretation.

The objector argues that stories of prophets committing sins contradict the doctrine of isma. This lesson presents the objector's claim and the first part of the general response, which distinguishes between solitary and mass-transmitted reports and explains why solitary reports are rejected outright.

Guided Path
1
Read the objector's claim
Read the opening lines where the objector cites prophetic stories as evidence against absolute infallibility. Note that the objector permits major sins forgetfully and minor sins intentionally after prophethood.
The objector uses both Quranic and hadith stories.
2
Identify the two categories of reports
The general answer separates reports into solitary (ahad) and mass-transmitted (mutawatir). Notice how each is treated differently.
Solitary reports are rejected; mutawatir reports are interpreted.
3
Understand the reasoning for rejecting solitary reports
Attributing error to narrators is considered easier than attributing sin to prophets. This is a key principle in defending isma.
4
See the principle for mutawatir reports
If a mutawatir report has another plausible interpretation, it is turned away from its apparent literal meaning to protect infallibility.
The proofs of infallibility (dala'il al-isma) guide this interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج المخالف ( الذاهب إلى جواز صدور الكبائر عنهم بعد البعثة سهوا وجواز الصغائر عمداً أيضاً ( بقصص الأنبياء التي نقلت في القرآن أو الأحاديث أو الآثار تلك وتلك القصص ( توهم صدور الذنب عنهم ) في زمان النبوة . ( والجواب : ) عن القصص ( إجمالاً) أن ما كان منها منقولاً بالآحاد وجب ردها لأن نسبة الخطأ إلى الرواة أهون من نسبة المعاصي إلى الأنبياء وما ثبت منها توتراً فما دام له محمل آخر حملناه عليه ونصرفه عن ظاهره لدلائل العصمة وما لم نجد له محيصا حملناه على أنه كان قبل البعثة (أو ( كان ) من قبيل ترك الأولى (أو ) من ( صغائر صدرت عنهم سهواً ولا ينفيه أي لا ينفي كونه من قبيل ترك الأولى أو الصغائر الصادرة سهوا (تسميته ذنباً في مثل قوله تعالى : ليغفر لك الله ما تقدم من ذنبك ﴾ [الفتح : 2 ]، ( ولا الاستغفار منه ولا الاعتراف بكونه ظلماً (منهم كما في قصة آدم عليه السلام يعني أن ) هذه الأمور الثلاثة لا تنافي المحملين الآخرين ( إذ لعل ذلك ) المذكور من التسمية والاستغفار والاعتراف (لعظمه ) عنهم أو ( عندهم) ألا ترى أن حسنات الأبرار سيئات المقربين فلذلك يسمى ترك الأولى منهم وكذا ارتكاب الصغيرة سهواً ذنباً ويستغفرون منه ويعترفون بكونه ظلماً ) أو أن ) أي أو لأن (قصدوا به هضماً أنفسهم وكسراً لها بأنها ارتكبت ذنباً يحتاج فيه إلى الاستغفار والاعتراف به على سبيل الابتهال والتضرع كي يعفو عنها وبها ( ومن جوز الصغائر عمداً فله زيادة فسحة) في الجواب إذ يزداد له وجه آخر وهو أن يقول : جاز أن يكون الصادر عنهم صغيرة عمداً لا كبيرة .
And the objector—who holds the permissibility of major sins occurring from them (prophets) after prophethood forgetfully and minor sins intentionally—argued using the stories of the prophets that are transmitted in the Quran, hadiths, or reports. Those stories give the impression that sin issued from them during the time of prophethood. The answer to the stories in general is: that which is transmitted via solitary reports must be rejected, because attributing error to the narrators is easier than attributing sins to the prophets. And what is established via tawatur (mass transmission), as long as it has another interpretation, we interpret it accordingly and turn it away from its literal meaning due to the proofs of infallibility. And if we find no way out, we interpret it as having occurred before prophethood, or as being of the type of leaving the better (tark al-awla), or as minor sins that issued from them forgetfully. And neither calling it a 'sin'—as in His statement: 'That Allah may forgive you your former sin' [al-Fath 2]—nor the seeking of forgiveness from it nor the admission of it being injustice (as in the story of Adam, peace be upon him) negates the other two interpretations. These three things do not contradict the other interpretations, because perhaps that naming, seeking forgiveness, and admission are due to its greatness in their view or according to them. Do you not see that the good deeds of the righteous are sins of the near ones? Hence leaving the better from them is called a sin, and similarly committing a minor sin forgetfully is called a sin, and they seek forgiveness from it and admit it as injustice. Or they intended thereby to humble themselves and to break themselves, as if they committed a sin requiring forgiveness and admission, in supplication and humility, so that He may pardon them for it. And whoever permits minor sins intentionally has more leeway in the answer, as another aspect arises: he may say that what issued from them could be a minor sin intentionally, not a major one.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage presents the objector's argument against absolute infallibility. The objector uses Quranic stories and hadiths that seem to show prophets committing sins after prophethood. The general answer (ijmalan) is then given. The answer distinguishes between solitary reports (ahad) and mass-transmitted (mutawatir) reports. Solitary reports are rejected because attributing error to narrators is easier than attributing sin to prophets. Mutawatir reports, if they have another possible interpretation, are interpreted accordingly to preserve isma. If no interpretation is found, they are explained as occurring before prophethood, as leaving the better (tark al-awla), or as minor sins forgetfully. The passage then addresses three potential counterarguments: the use of the word 'sin' for such acts, the prophets seeking forgiveness, and their admitting injustice. These do not contradict the interpretations, because such acts are considered sins from their high station relative to the nearness of prophets; what is a minor fault for others is significant for them. Alternatively, they may lower themselves in humility. Finally, those who allow minor sins intentionally have an additional option: they can maintain that the act was a minor sin intentionally, not a major one.

Key Terms
المخالف
قصص الأنبياء
آحاد
متواتر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why are solitary reports rejected in the general answer?
A) Because they are always false.
B) Because attributing error to narrators is easier than attributing sin to prophets.
C) Because they contradict the Quran.
D) Because they are not mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
Solitary reports are rejected to protect prophetic infallibility, while mutawatir reports are interpreted in a compatible way.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever dismissed or doubted a hadith because it seemed to conflict with the belief in prophetic infallibility? What was your reasoning, and did you consider the principle that error in narrators is easier than sin in the prophets?
?
When you read a Qur'anic story that appears to show a prophet sinning, do you immediately seek an interpretation that preserves their honor, or do you allow the literal meaning to unsettle your heart? What does your habit reveal about your faith in Allah's choice of messengers?
?
If a solitary report challenged a belief you hold dear, are you willing to side with the possibility of narrator error over the prophet's perfection? How does this lesson shape your approach to adopting beliefs from hadith?

Three Fallback Interpretations for Prophetic Stories
Sanusi provides three interpretations for mutawatir stories and addresses that naming them sins does not contradict infallibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three interpretations for mutawatir prophetic stories that cannot be otherwise explained: before prophethood, leaving the better, or minor sins forgetfully.

Core Idea
When no alternative interpretation exists, prophetic stories are understood as before prophethood, leaving the better, or minor forgetful sins.

After establishing that mutawatir reports should be interpreted, Sanusi provides three fallback explanations for stories that still appear problematic. This lesson covers those interpretations and also addresses the potential objection that such acts are called 'sin' in the Quran, showing that calling them sin does not contradict these interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Read the three fallback interpretations
Locate the three cases: before prophethood, leaving the better (tark al-awla), and minor sins forgetfully. Understand each category.
These are only used when no other interpretation is possible.
2
Note the three counterarguments
The passage then addresses three things that might seem to contradict the fallback interpretations: calling the act a 'sin', seeking forgiveness, and admitting it as injustice.
These are illustrated by Quranic verses like al-Fath 2 and the story of Adam.
3
Understand why counterarguments do not negate the interpretations
Sanusi argues that these three things are not contradictory because the act being called a sin, etc., does not rule out that it was tark al-awla or a minor forgetful sin.
The key is that such acts are considered sins from the prophets' high station.

?

?

In your own spiritual life, are you too quick to label your own failings as 'major' (leading to despair) or 'minor' (leading to complacency)? Why Are These Called Sins? Explanations and Extra Leeway
Sanusi explains why prophets call minor faults sins and provides an extra answer for those who permit intentional minor sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two explanations for why prophets' minor faults are called sins or lead to istighfar, and the extra leeway available to those who permit minor sins intentionally.

Core Idea
Prophets call their minor faults 'sins' due to their high status or as an act of humility; those allowing minor sins have an additional answer.

The previous lesson showed that calling an act a sin does not contradict infallibility. This lesson explains why prophets themselves use such language – either because even minor faults are significant for them, or as a form of humility. Finally, Sanusi notes that those who permit minor sins intentionally have another option to defend prophetic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the two explanations for using 'sin' language
The passage gives two reasons: either because the act is considered great in the eyes of the prophets (due to their high station), or because they humble themselves by calling it a sin.
The example 'the good deeds of the righteous are sins of the near ones' illustrates the first explanation.
2
Understand the humility explanation
Prophets may intentionally humble themselves, treating minor faults as if they were sins requiring forgiveness and admission, in order to supplicate and draw closer to Allah.
3
Note the extra leeway for those who allow minor sins intentionally
If one holds that minor sins can be committed intentionally by prophets, there is an additional response: the act in question could be a minor sin intentionally, not a major one.
This gives more flexibility in interpreting the stories.

Source Text

?

?

Six Aspects of Adam's Story: Defending Prophetic Isma
Detailed answer listing four of six objections from Adam's story and a possible interpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how scholars interpret the story of Adam (AS) to defend prophetic isma (sinlessness) against objections from apparent disobedience.

Core Idea
Disobedience in Adam's story can be interpreted as leaving the better, not sin.

After summarizing the objectors' use of prophetic stories, the author now details the strongest example: Adam's story. He lists six aspects that opponents use to claim Adam sinned, then provides answers. We will examine four of these aspects and the key interpretive principle that resolves them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the full literal translation to grasp the author's argument.
The passage is incomplete; only four of six aspects are listed.
2
Identify the four listed aspects
The text explicitly numbers the first four aspects: (1) 'Adam disobeyed his Lord' and 'went astray,' (2) repentance implies sin, (3) violation of a prohibition, (4) being called 'wrongdoers.'
Each aspect is a different verse from the Quran.
3
Understand the interpretive possibility for the first aspect
After listing the fourth aspect, the author presents a possible answer: the prohibition in the story might have been for recommendation (nadb) and dispreference (tanzih), not obligation. Thus, leaving it is not a major sin.
This interpretation preserves Adam's sinlessness.
4
Consider how this protects isma
Reflect on how interpreting the prohibition as recommendatory removes the claim that Adam committed a major sin. This shows the importance of proper understanding of Quranic commands.
This is a key method in defending prophetic infallibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولنفصل ما أجملناه من استدلال المخالف بالقصص المنقولة . وجوابنا عنه ( تفصيلاً فمنه ) أي من ذلك المحمل ( قصة آدم عليه السلام وتفيقهوا) أي تكلموا بملء أفواههم ( في التمسك بها من ستة أوجه : الأول : قوله تعالى: ﴿ و عصی آدم ربه ﴾ [ طه : 121 ] ، مؤكداً بقوله : (فغوى فإن العصيان من الكبائر بدليل قوله تعالى : ومن يعص الله ورسوله فإن له نار جهنم ﴾ [الجن: 23]، والغواية تؤكد ذلك لأنها اتباع الشيطان لقوله تعالى : إلا من اتبعك من الغاوين ﴾ [ الحجر : 42. ( الثاني : قوله تعالى : فتاب عليه ﴾ [البقرة : 37]، ولن تكون التوبة إلا عن الذنب ) لأنها الندم على المعصية والعزيمة على ترك العود إليها . ( الثالث : مخالفته النهي عن أكل الشجرة وارتكاب المنهي عنه ذنب . ( الرابع : قوله تعالى : فتكونا من الظالمين ﴾ [البقرة : 35] جعلهما الله من الظالمين على تقدير الأكل منها والظلم قوله : (الأول قوله تعالى : وعصى آدم ربه ﴾ [طه: 121] (الآية) قيل: يحتمل أن يكون النهي في قوله تعالى: ﴿ ولا تقربا هذه الشجرة ﴾ [البقرة : 35] للندب والتنزيه وترك المندوب مثله عصياناً وغواية وظلماً .
Let us detail what we summarized of the objector's argument using the transmitted stories. Our answer in detail: among the interpretations is the story of Adam, peace be upon him. They spoke with full mouths in clinging to it from six aspects: First: His statement, the Exalted: 'And Adam disobeyed his Lord' [Ta Ha 121], emphasized by His statement: 'and went astray.' For disobedience is among the major sins, as evidenced by His statement: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, indeed for him is the fire of Hell' [al-Jinn 23]. And going astray confirms that because it is following Satan, as per His statement: 'except those who follow you from among the astray' [al-Hijr 42]. Second: His statement: 'Then He accepted his repentance' [al-Baqarah 37], and repentance is only due to sin, because it is regret for disobedience and determination not to return to it. Third: His violation of the prohibition from eating the tree, and committing the prohibited is a sin. Fourth: His statement: 'Then you would be among the wrongdoers' [al-Baqarah 35], Allah made them wrongdoers on the condition of eating from it, and wrongdoing is ... He said: (The first: His statement: 'And Adam disobeyed his Lord' [Ta Ha 121]) It was said: It is possible that the prohibition in His statement: 'And do not approach this tree' [al-Baqarah 35] was for recommendation and dispreference, and leaving the recommended is called disobedience, straying, and wrongdoing.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed answer (tafsilan) to the objector's use of prophetic stories, focusing on Adam's story as the strongest example. The objector holds six aspects to prove sin from Adam's story. Four are listed: (1) The Quran says 'Adam disobeyed his Lord and went astray,' and disobedience is a major sin, as per the threat of Hell. (2) Repentance implies prior sin, since repentance is regret for disobedience. (3) Adam violated a clear prohibition, which is a sin. (4) Adam was called a 'wrongdoer' (zalim) for eating, and wrongdoing is sin. The text then presents a possible interpretation for the first aspect: the prohibition might be for recommendation (nadb) and dispreference (tanzih), not obligation, so leaving the recommended is called disobedience and straying in a figurative sense. The passage cuts off before listing the fifth and sixth aspects, presumably interrupted by page break.

Key Terms

عصیان
غواية
توبة
نهي
ظالمين
ندب
تنزيه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any act described as 'disobedience' or 'wrongdoing' in the Quran must be a major sin.
Correction: The author shows that such terms can be used figuratively when a recommended act is left, as in the case of Adam's prohibition understood as recommendatory.

Checkpoint
What is a possible interpretation of the prohibition in the story of Adam according to the author?
A) It was an absolute prohibition showing sin.
B) It was a recommendation, not an obligation.
C) It was a test with no moral weight.
D) It was meant only for Adam, not his wife.

Key Takeaway
The story of Adam (AS) can be harmonized with prophetic isma by understanding the prohibition as recommendatory, not absolute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Adam's action is called 'disobedience' and 'straying' yet could be leaving the better, does your heart immediately want to defend the literal reading or accept the possibility? Which tendency are you more prone to—demanding absolute literalness or embracing interpretive mercy? Will you commit to pausing before condemning others' actions that seem wrong, remembering that there may be a valid interpretation you haven't considered?
?
The objector used powerful Quranic verses to claim that Prophets can sin. How often do you weaponize religious texts to judge or dismiss others, forgetting that the same texts can be interpreted in ways that preserve honor and mercy? What specific relationship or situation in your life needs this lesson right now?
?
Adam's repentance was accepted even if his 'disobedience' was only leaving the better. Are you holding yourself to a standard of perfection that denies the possibility of sincere repentance for minor failings? Will you today stop labeling your small missteps as unforgivable and instead turn to Allah with humility, trusting that He accepts even the return from a lesser good to a greater good?

Rejecting Ahad Reports on Prophetic Sin
Sanusi states the rule for dealing with solitary reports (ahad) that imply prophetic sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why solitary reports (ahad) that seem to indicate prophetic sins must be rejected and the reasoning behind this principle.

Core Idea
Attributing error to narrators is easier than attributing sin to prophets.

The issue of stories suggesting prophetic sins requires a careful methodology. The first principle concerns the reliability of the transmission: reports that are not mass-transmitted (mutawatir) cannot override the definitive proofs of infallibility. In this lesson, we explore the rationale for rejecting such reports.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on ahad reports
Read the Arabic and translation carefully. Notice that the principle is stated briefly: ahad reports must be rejected.
2
Understand the reasoning
The reason given is that error in narrators is a lesser problem than attributing sin to prophets. Reflect on this principle of harm minimization.
This is a key rule in kalam: the more serious implication is avoided.
3
Apply the principle
Consider a hypothetical story from an ahad hadith that contradicts infallibility. How would this principle guide your response?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الأول - المقصد الخامس : في عصمة الأنبياء الصغائر عمداً أيضاً ( بقصص الأنبياء التي نقلت في القرآن أو الأحاديث أو الآثار تلك وتلك القصص ( توهم صدور الذنب عنهم ) في زمان النبوة . ( والجواب : ) عن القصص ( إجمالاً) أن ما كان منها منقولاً بالآحاد وجب ردها لأن نسبة الخطأ إلى الرواة من أهون من نسبة المعاصي إلى الأنبياء وما ثبت منها توتراً فما دام له محمل آخر حملناه عليه ونصرفه عن ظاهره لدلائل العصمة وما لم نجد له محيصا حملناه على أنه كان قبل البعثة (أو ( كان ) من قبيل ترك الأولى (أو ) من ( صغائر صدرت عنهم سهواً ولا ينفيه أي لا ينفي كونه من قبيل ترك الأولى أو الصغائر الصادرة سهوا (تسميته ذنباً في مثل قوله تعالى : ليغفر لك الله ما تقدم من ذنبك ﴾ [الفتح : ٢ ]، ( ولا الاستغفار منه ولا الاعتراف بكونه ظلماً (منهم كما في قصة آدم عليه السلام يعني أن ) هذه الأمور الثلاثة لا تنافي المحملين الآخرين ( إذ لعل ذلك ) المذكور من التسمية والاستغفار والاعتراف (لعظمه ) عنهم أو ( عندهم) ألا ترى أن حسنات الأبرار سيئات المقربين فلذلك يسمى ترك الأولى منهم وكذا ارتكاب الصغيرة سهواً ذنباً ويستغفرون منه ويعترفون بكونه ظلماً ) أو أن ) أي أو لأن (قصدوا به هضماً أنفسهم وكسراً لها بأنها ارتكبت ذنباً يحتاج فيه إلى الاستغفار والاعتراف به على سبيل الابتهال والتضرع كي يعفو عنها وبها ( ومن جوز الصغائر عمداً فله زيادة فسحة) في الجواب إذ يزداد له وجه آخر وهو أن يقول : جاز أن يكون الصادر عنهم صغيرة عمداً لا كبيرة )
The First Observatory - The Fifth Objective: On the Infallibility of the Prophets. Minor sins intentionally as well (by stories of the prophets that have been transmitted in the Qur'an or hadiths or traditions. Those stories (give the impression that sin occurred from them) in the time of prophethood. (And the answer:) concerning the stories (in summary) that what is transmitted by solitary reports must be rejected because attributing error to the narrators is easier than attributing sins to the prophets. And what is established by mutawatir transmission, as long as it has another interpretation, we interpret it upon that and divert it from its apparent meaning due to the proofs of infallibility. And what we find no escape from, we interpret it as having occurred before the mission (or (being) of the type of leaving the better (or) of (minor sins that occurred from them forgetfully). And it does not negate, i.e., does not negate its being of the type of leaving the better or minor sins occurring forgetfully (calling it a sin in such as His statement: 'That Allah may forgive you what is past of your sin' [48:2], (nor seeking forgiveness from it nor admitting it being injustice (from them as in the story of Adam, peace be upon him, meaning that) these three matters do not contradict the other two interpretations. (For perhaps that) mentioned of naming, seeking forgiveness, and admission (due to its enormity) from them or (in their view). Do you not see that the good deeds of the pious are sins of those brought near? Therefore leaving the better from them is called a sin, and likewise committing a minor sin forgetfully is called a sin, and they seek forgiveness from it and admit it being injustice. (Or that) i.e., or because (they intended by it self-abasement and breaking of themselves, as if they had committed a sin requiring seeking forgiveness and admission by way of supplication and humility so that He may pardon them and by it. (And whoever permits minor sins intentionally has an additional latitude) in the answer, for another aspect is added for him: that it is possible that what issued from them was a minor sin intentionally, not a major sin.)
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage defines the general methodology for responding to scriptural stories that appear to show prophets committing sins. The author begins by stating the problem: stories from the Qur'an, hadith, and historical reports may give the impression that sins occurred from prophets during their prophetic period. The answer is given in two parts: for reports transmitted by solitary chains (ahaad), they must be rejected because it is easier to attribute error to the narrators than to attribute sin to prophets. For reports that are mutawatir (mass-transmitted), as long as another interpretation is possible, the apparent meaning is diverted due to the definitive proofs of prophetic infallibility. If no interpretation is found, the incident is interpreted as having occurred before their prophetic mission, or as being of the type of 'leaving the better' (tark al-awlaa), or as minor sins committed forgetfully. The author then explains that calling such acts 'sins', seeking forgiveness for them, or admitting them as injustice does not contradict the interpretations of 'leaving the better' or forgetful minor sin. This is because such acts are considered sins due to their greatness in the eyes of the prophets, akin to the principle that the good deeds of the pious are sins of those brought near to God. The passage ends by noting that for those who allow minor sins intentionally, there is an additional answer: the act could have been a minor sin committed intentionally, not a major one.

Key Terms
آحاد
عصمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any story in Islamic sources that seems to show a prophet sinning must be accepted as factual.
Correction: The passage explains that the method of transmission is crucial. Solitary reports (ahad) are rejected outright because error in transmission is easier to accept than sin in prophets.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why must solitary reports (ahad) that seem to indicate prophetic sin be rejected?
A) Because they are weak in authenticity.
B) Because attributing error to narrators is easier than attributing sin to prophets.
C) Because they contradict the Qur'an.
D) Because the prophets themselves rejected them.

Key Takeaway
Solitary reports (ahad) that seem to indicate prophetic sin are rejected because it is easier to assume error in transmission than to charge a prophet with sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you come across a report that makes you doubt the character of a prophet, do you instinctively accept it or do you immediately question its transmission? What will you do next time?
?
The principle here is 'it is easier to blame the narrator than the prophet.' Where in your own life do you find yourself quick to assume the worst about someone else rather than consider a flaw in the source of your information? How can you apply this same principle of caution?
?
This lesson forces you to prioritize the honor of prophets over the apparent validity of a story. Is there a belief or attitude you hold that would crumble if you applied the same standard—protecting what Allah has sanctified even when facts seem to contradict? Are you willing to surrender that assumption?

Interpreting Mutawatir Reports about Prophetic Sin
Sanusi outlines three ways to interpret mutawatir reports that suggest prophetic sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three acceptable interpretations for mutawatir reports that appear to show prophetic sin: before prophethood, leaving the better, or forgetful minor sins.

Core Idea
Mutawatir reports are reinterpreted, not rejected.

For reports that are mass-transmitted (mutawatir) and thus cannot be dismissed as unreliable, we must find alternative interpretations that preserve infallibility. This lesson presents the three standard options scholars use.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on mutawatir reports
Read the part dealing with reports that are mutawatir. Notice the three options listed.
2
Understand each option
The three options are: before prophethood, leaving the better (tark al-awla), and minor sins committed forgetfully. Reflect on how each preserves infallibility.
3
Recognize the priority
The passage says: as long as there is any other interpretation, we divert from the apparent meaning. This shows the strong commitment to infallibility.

Source Text

?

?

Identify one habit where you consistently take the easy permissible path instead of the excellent one. What would change if you intentionally pursued the higher choice for the next seven days?
?
You give the benefit of the doubt to the Prophet (s) by reinterpreting reports. Do you extend the same charity to other Muslims when you hear something negative about them? This principle of seeking alternative interpretations can transform your relationships. Think of one person you have misjudged recently. Can you find a possible good interpretation for their action? Resolve to ask them or give them an excuse before concluding ill.

Why 'Sin', 'Seeking Forgiveness', and 'Admission' Are Compatible with Prophetic Infallibility
Sanusi explains that calling an act 'sin', seeking forgiveness, and admitting injustice do not conflict with the interpretations of leaving the better or forgetful minor sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that calling an act a 'sin', seeking forgiveness, or admitting it as injustice does not necessarily imply it is a genuine sin that violates infallibility; it can be a case of 'leaving the better' or forgetful minor sin, considered sin due to the prophet's high station.

Core Idea
Good deeds of the pious are sins of the near ones.

One might object that if a prophet's action is interpreted as 'leaving the better' or a forgetful minor sin, why does the Qur'an call it a 'sin' and mention forgiveness? This lesson resolves that by showing that these terms are used due to the elevated status of prophets.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on terminology
Read the Arabic and translation regarding the three matters: naming it a sin, seeking forgiveness, and admitting injustice.
2
Reflect on the key principle
The principle 'good deeds of the pious are sins of the near ones' shows that actions are evaluated relative to the actor's rank. What is fine for an ordinary person is a sin for a prophet.
3
Consider the additional explanation
The passage also suggests that prophets might use such language to humble themselves. Also, note the extra latitude for those who allow minor sins intentionally.

And what is established by mutawatir transmission, as long as it has another interpretation, we interpret it upon that and divert it from its apparent meaning due to the proofs of infallibility. And what we find no escape from, we interpret it as having occurred before the mission (or (being) of the type of leaving the better (or) of (minor sins that occurred from them forgetfully). And it does not negate, i.e., does not negate its being of the type of leaving the better or minor sins occurring forgetfully (calling it a sin in such as His statement: 'That Allah may forgive you what is past of your sin' [48:2], (nor seeking forgiveness from it nor admitting it being injustice (from them as in the story of Adam, peace be upon him, meaning that) these three matters do not contradict the other two interpretations. (For perhaps that) mentioned of naming, seeking forgiveness, and admission (due to its enormity) from them or (in their view). Do you not see that the good deeds of the pious are sins of those brought near? Therefore leaving the better from them is called a sin, and likewise committing a minor sin forgetfully is called a sin, and they seek forgiveness from it and admit it being injustice. (Or that) i.e., or because (they intended by it self-abasement and breaking of themselves, as if they had committed a sin requiring seeking forgiveness and admission by way of supplication and humility so that He may pardon them and by it. (And whoever permits minor sins intentionally has an additional latitude) in the answer, for another aspect is added for him: that it is possible that what issued from them was a minor sin intentionally, not a major sin.)
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage defines the general methodology for responding to scriptural stories that appear to show prophets committing sins. The author begins by stating the problem: stories from the Qur'an, hadith, and historical reports may give the impression that sins occurred from prophets during their prophetic period. The answer is given in two parts: for reports transmitted by solitary chains (ahaad), they must be rejected because it is easier to attribute error to the narrators than to attribute sin to prophets. For reports that are mutawatir (mass-transmitted), as long as another interpretation is possible, the apparent meaning is diverted due to the definitive proofs of prophetic infallibility. If no interpretation is found, the incident is interpreted as having occurred before their prophetic mission, or as being of the type of 'leaving the better' (tark al-awlaa), or as minor sins committed forgetfully. The author then explains that calling such acts 'sins', seeking forgiveness for them, or admitting them as injustice does not contradict the interpretations of 'leaving the better' or forgetful minor sin. This is because such acts are considered sins due to their greatness in the eyes of the prophets, akin to the principle that the good deeds of the pious are sins of those brought near to God. The passage ends by noting that for those who allow minor sins intentionally, there is an additional answer: the act could have been a minor sin committed intentionally, not a major one.

Key Terms
ذنب
توبة
استغفار
ظلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If the Qur'an calls something a 'sin' and mentions forgiveness, it must be a genuine sin that violates infallibility.
Correction: The passage explains that such terminology can be used for 'leaving the better' or forgetful minor sins due to the prophets' elevated status or for self-humbling.

Checkpoint
What principle does the author invoke to explain that 'leaving the better' can be called a sin?
A) The good deeds of the pious are sins of the near ones.
B) Every sin must be punished.
C) Prophets are infallible from all sins.
D) The Qur'an is allegorical.

Key Takeaway
Calling an act a 'sin' or seeking forgiveness does not contradict the interpretations of leaving the better or forgetful minor sin, due to the prophets' high station and humility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever belittled a small mistake of yours as 'insignificant' when, compared to the Prophet's station, even leaving the better is called a sin? How can you recalibrate your conscience to take every wrong seriously?
?
When you seek forgiveness, do you truly humble yourself before Allah, or do you recite words without feeling the weight of your shortcomings? How can you practice the self-abasement (هضماً لأنفسكم) that the prophets showed?
?
If the best of creation admitted injustice to break their ego, what prevents you from confessing your faults to Allah with the same sincerity? Write down one fault you haven't admitted and then say istighfar with that spirit.

Six Arguments from Adam's Story
The author enumerates six arguments from the story of Adam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six specific scriptural arguments that opponents use from the story of Adam to challenge prophetic infallibility.

Core Idea
Critics use six Quranic phrases from Adam's story to argue he sinned.

The author promised to detail the arguments drawn from prophetic stories. Here he presents six distinct verses from the story of Adam that opponents claim demonstrate his sin. Each argument interprets a specific Quranic phrase to support that Adam committed a major sin, which would contradict the doctrine of prophetic infallibility. Pay close attention to how each argument is constructed from the text.

Guided Path
1
Read the introduction and six arguments
Read the Arabic passage slowly. Notice the numbered structure and how each argument cites a specific verse.
2
Identify the common thread
Each argument focuses on a different word: 'disobeyed', 'repented', 'wrongdoers', etc. What do they all have in common?
All are taken as evidence of sin.
3
Reflect on the strength of each argument
Consider how compelling each argument seems before reading the refutation.
The refutation will introduce context.
4
Prepare for the refutation
Keep in mind that the author will respond by saying Adam was not yet a prophet.

And let us detail what we summarized of the opponent's argument by the transmitted stories. (The second: His statement, exalted is He: 'Then He relented upon him' [2:37], and repentance is only from sin, because it is regret for disobedience and resolve to not return to it. (The third: his violation of the prohibition from eating the tree and committing the prohibited is a sin. (The fourth: His statement, exalted is He: 'Then you would be of the wrongdoers' [2:35]; He made them from the wrongdoers on the condition of eating from it, and wrongdoing is a sin. A sin. (The fifth: His statement, exalted is He: (narrating from them) 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves, and if You do not forgive us and have mercy upon us, we will surely be among the losers' [7:23], and wrongdoing is a sin as just mentioned, and loss without forgiveness is evidence of it being a major sin. (The sixth: His statement, exalted is He: 'So Satan caused them to slip from it and brought them out from what they were in' [2:36], and deserving of expulsion due to Satan's causing them to slip indicates that what issued from them was a major sin. (We said: (in the answer) How is it claimed that he was in paradise and he had no nation there (was he a prophet) sent to convey rulings? And was the choice for prophethood except after that story? As indicated by His statement: 'So he went astray, then his Lord chose him, then He relented upon him' [20:121-122], for the word 'then' indicates delay and interval; so this story was before prophethood. (And is the attack) i.e., the criticism (against the prophets by such an argument whose refutation is apparent except due to blindness) and confusion in misguidance and excessive ignorance in error. His statement: (And he has no nation (this is an intervening sentence and the news of his statement 'he was a prophet' and in it is a discussion, namely that His statement: 'Settle, you and your wife, in Paradise and eat from it abundantly wherever you wish and do not approach this tree' [2:35] indicates that revelation came to him before his exit from Paradise, so it indicates his prophethood therein. It cannot be said: Revelation does not necessarily entail prophethood, by His statement: 'And We inspired to the mother of Moses to nurse him' [28:7] since a woman is not conceived to be a prophet. For we say: What is understood from what has been narrated concerning Adam, peace be upon him, from the verses is hearing organized speech while awake, which is called apparent revelation and recited revelation, and that has not been established for other than a prophet; rather, that is perhaps made a characteristic of the messenger. As for the casting of meaning into the heart while awake or hearing speech in a dream, which is called revelation and inspiration linguistically, and that is what is intended by what has been narrated concerning the mother of Moses, peace be upon him, as clarified in books of interpretation, it is not exclusive to him at all. And as for his having no nation in Paradise, it may be answered that Eve was a nation for him. It is replied that sending to a single person is not customary. Hence they said in the definition of a prophet: he is one to whom Allah says: 'We have sent you to the people' or 'to such and such people.' And it can be rebutted that what is not customary is sending to a single person only. And the mentioned definition does not require that the people sent to exist at the beginning of the sending. For there is no doubt that some who are born after the sending enter into it absolutely. So Adam, peace be upon him, it is possible that he was sent to Eve and her children, and the one present at the beginning of the sending was Eve only. However, it is said in 'Lubab al-Arba'in': If Adam, peace be upon him, was a messenger before the incident, he would have been a messenger without anyone sent to, because there was no human in Paradise other than Eve, and the address was to her without the mediation of Adam, peace be upon him, by His statement: 'And do not approach' [2:35], and the angels are messengers of Allah, so they do not need another messenger. And you are well aware that what he mentioned indicates that the mentioned revelation necessitates prophethood, even though they explicitly stated that his prophethood, peace be upon him, was established by the Book. So the closest is that the address without mediation was to Adam, peace be upon him. And as for His statement: 'And do not approach' [2:35], it is by way of overriding inclusion (taghleeb), as established in rhetorical sciences. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed refutation of six specific arguments drawn from the story of Adam (AS) that opponents use to challenge prophetic infallibility. The author first introduces that he will detail the opponent's arguments and the response. The six aspects are enumerated: 1) the verse 'And Adam disobeyed his Lord' (20:121) confirmed by 'and went astray,' with the claim that disobedience is a major sin; 2) the verse 'Then He relented upon him' (2:37) implying repentance from sin; 3) Adam's violation of the prohibition against eating the tree; 4) the verse 'then you would be of the wrongdoers' (2:35) and that wrongdoing is a sin; 5) Adam and Eve's statement 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves' (7:23) and the threat of loss without forgiveness; 6) the verse 'So Satan caused them to slip' (2:36) indicating expulsion due to a major sin. The author then gives the answer: how can it be claimed that Adam was in paradise—he had no nation there, so was he a prophet sent to convey rulings? Moreover, the choice for prophethood occurred after that story, as indicated by the word 'then' (thumma) in 'So he went astray, then his Lord chose him, then He relented upon him' (20:121-122), showing the story was before prophethood. Attacking prophets with such a flimsy argument is only due to blindness and ignorance. The passage then includes a long discussion about whether Adam could have been a prophet in paradise, addressing the objection that revelation to Adam in paradise implies prophethood. The author distinguishes between the type of revelation given to Adam (recited, while awake) and that given to the mother of Moses (inner inspiration), showing that Adam's revelation was exclusive to prophets. Regarding the objection that Adam had no nation in paradise, possible answers are discussed: Eve could be his nation, or the definition of a prophet does not require the people to exist at the time of sending. The discussion concludes that the closest view is that the direct address was to Adam, and the dual address in (2:35) is by way of taghleeb (overriding inclusion).

The Refutation: Adam Was Not Yet a Prophet
The author refutes the six arguments and discusses prophethood in paradise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the main refutation to the six arguments: that the incident occurred before Adam's prophethood, and the subsequent discussion about revelation and nation.

Core Idea
Adam's story happened before he became a prophet, so it does not affect prophetic infallibility.

After listing the six arguments, the author now provides the decisive answer. He argues that the incident in paradise took place before Adam was appointed a prophet, as indicated by the word 'then' (thumma) in the verse. This refutation is further supported by a detailed discussion about the nature of revelation Adam received and whether he had a 'nation' in paradise. Read carefully to see how each objection is countered.

Guided Path
1
Read the core response
Focus on the opening answer: 'How can it be claimed that he was in paradise and he had no nation there, was he a prophet?'
2
Understand the 'thumma' argument
The verse 'Then his Lord chose him' uses the word 'then' which indicates delay, placing the story before prophethood.
3
Examine the revelation discussion
The author distinguishes between the type of revelation given to Adam (recited, waking speech) and that given to others like the mother of Moses (inner inspiration).
This shows Adam's revelation was prophetic.
4
Consider the 'nation' objection
The author addresses the claim that Adam had no nation: Eve could be considered his nation, and the definition of a prophet does not require the people to exist at the start.

And let us detail what we summarized of the opponent's argument by the transmitted stories. And our answer about it (in detail): among it, i.e., among that interpretation, (is the story of Adam, peace be upon him, and they spoke with full mouths i.e., they spoke with their mouths full, in clinging to it from six aspects. The first: His statement, exalted is He: 'And Adam disobeyed his Lord' [20:121], confirmed by His statement: 'And went astray,' for disobedience is from the major sins, evidenced by His statement: 'And whoever disobeys Allah and His Messenger, then indeed for him is the fire of Hell' [72:23], and going astray confirms that because it is following Satan, by His statement: 'except those who follow you from the astray ones' [15:42]. (The second: His statement, exalted is He: 'Then He relented upon him' [2:37], and repentance is only from sin, because it is regret for disobedience and resolve to not return to it. (The third: his violation of the prohibition from eating the tree and committing the prohibited is a sin. (The fourth: His statement, exalted is He: 'Then you would be of the wrongdoers' [2:35]; He made them from the wrongdoers on the condition of eating from it, and wrongdoing is a sin. It is said: It is possible that the prohibition in His statement: 'And do not approach this tree' [2:35] was for recommendation and betterment, and leaving the recommended is like it: disobedience, going astray, and wrongdoing. A sin. (The fifth: His statement, exalted is He: (narrating from them) 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves, and if You do not forgive us and have mercy upon us, we will surely be among the losers' [7:23], and wrongdoing is a sin as just mentioned, and loss without forgiveness is evidence of it being a major sin. (The sixth: His statement, exalted is He: 'So Satan caused them to slip from it and brought them out from what they were in' [2:36], and deserving of expulsion due to Satan's causing them to slip indicates that what issued from them was a major sin. (We said: (in the answer) How is it claimed that he was in paradise and he had no nation there (was he a prophet) sent to convey rulings? And was the choice for prophethood except after that story? As indicated by His statement: 'So he went astray, then his Lord chose him, then He relented upon him' [20:121-122], for the word 'then' indicates delay and interval; so this story was before prophethood. (And is the attack) i.e., the criticism (against the prophets by such an argument whose refutation is apparent except due to blindness) and confusion in misguidance and excessive ignorance in error. (And some may cling regarding his sin) i.e., the sin of Adam (to His statement: 'It is He who created you from one soul' [39:6] which is Adam.

It cannot be said: Revelation does not necessarily entail prophethood, by His statement: 'And We inspired to the mother of Moses to nurse him' [28:7] since a woman is not conceived to be a prophet. For we say: What is understood from what has been narrated concerning Adam, peace be upon him, from the verses is hearing organized speech while awake, which is called apparent revelation and recited revelation, and that has not been established for other than a prophet; rather, that is perhaps made a characteristic of the messenger. As for the casting of meaning into the heart while awake or hearing speech in a dream, which is called revelation and inspiration linguistically, and that is what is intended by what has been narrated concerning the mother of Moses, peace be upon him, as clarified in books of interpretation, it is not exclusive to him at all. And as for his having no nation in Paradise, it may be answered that Eve was a nation for him. It is replied that sending to a single person is not customary. Hence they said in the definition of a prophet: he is one to whom Allah says: 'We have sent you to the people' or 'to such and such people.' And it can be rebutted that what is not customary is sending to a single person only. And the mentioned definition does not require that the people sent to exist at the beginning of the sending. For there is no doubt that some who are born after the sending enter into it absolutely. So Adam, peace be upon him, it is possible that he was sent to Eve and her children, and the one present at the beginning of the sending was Eve only. However, it is said in 'Lubab al-Arba'in': If Adam, peace be upon him, was a messenger before the incident, he would have been a messenger without anyone sent to, because there was no human in Paradise other than Eve, and the address was to her without the mediation of Adam, peace be upon him, by His statement: 'And do not approach' [2:35], and the angels are messengers of Allah, so they do not need another messenger. And you are well aware that what he mentioned indicates that the mentioned revelation necessitates prophethood, even though they explicitly stated that his prophethood, peace be upon him, was established by the Book. So the closest is that the address without mediation was to Adam, peace be upon him. And as for His statement: 'And do not approach' [2:35], it is by way of overriding inclusion (taghleeb), as established in rhetorical sciences. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed refutation of six specific arguments drawn from the story of Adam (AS) that opponents use to challenge prophetic infallibility. The author first introduces that he will detail the opponent's arguments and the response. The six aspects are enumerated: 1) the verse 'And Adam disobeyed his Lord' (20:121) confirmed by 'and went astray,' with the claim that disobedience is a major sin; 2) the verse 'Then He relented upon him' (2:37) implying repentance from sin; 3) Adam's violation of the prohibition against eating the tree; 4) the verse 'then you would be of the wrongdoers' (2:35) and that wrongdoing is a sin; 5) Adam and Eve's statement 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves' (7:23) and the threat of loss without forgiveness; 6) the verse 'So Satan caused them to slip' (2:36) indicating expulsion due to a major sin. The author then gives the answer: how can it be claimed that Adam was in paradise—he had no nation there, so was he a prophet sent to convey rulings? Moreover, the choice for prophethood occurred after that story, as indicated by the word 'then' (thumma) in 'So he went astray, then his Lord chose him, then He relented upon him' (20:121-122), showing the story was before prophethood. Attacking prophets with such a flimsy argument is only due to blindness and ignorance. The passage then includes a long discussion about whether Adam could have been a prophet in paradise, addressing the objection that revelation to Adam in paradise implies prophethood. The author distinguishes between the type of revelation given to Adam (recited, while awake) and that given to the mother of Moses (inner inspiration), showing that Adam's revelation was exclusive to prophets. Regarding the objection that Adam had no nation in paradise, possible answers are discussed: Eve could be his nation, or the definition of a prophet does not require the people to exist at the time of sending. The discussion concludes that the closest view is that the direct address was to Adam, and the dual address in (2:35) is by way of taghleeb (overriding inclusion).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The story of Adam proves he committed a major sin, which contradicts prophetic infallibility.
Correction: The incident occurred before Adam was a prophet, as the Quranic word 'then' shows. Thus, it does not affect the infallibility of prophets.

Checkpoint
What is the main evidence used in the refutation to show that the story of Adam occurred before his prophethood?
A) The word 'then' (ثم) in the verse 'Then his Lord chose him'
B) The verse 'And We inspired to the mother of Moses'
C) The fact that Adam had no nation
D) The definition of a prophet

Key Takeaway
The story of Adam does not challenge prophetic infallibility because it happened before he became a prophet.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at your own life, are you honest about the times you have fallen into sin before truly submitting to Allah? What would it mean for you to see your past mistakes as pre-prophethood moments—opportunities for ijtiba and transformation, not permanent failures?
?
The author condemns those who attack the prophets with weak arguments. In your own conversations about Islam, do you sometimes rely on weak reasoning or emotional arguments that could be easily refuted? Are you willing to study deeply so that your faith is built on solid proofs, not just feelings?
?
Adam heard Allah directly. Yet you have His final revelation—the Qur’an. When you read it, do you truly listen as if He is speaking to you personally, or do you let distractions and desires drown out His call? What concrete step will you take today to give the Qur’an the attention it deserves?

Answering the Objection of Major Sin
Al-Jurjani presents the fifth and sixth objections and gives the main response that the sin preceded prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the objections based on Adam's confession of wrongdoing and expulsion are invalid because they occurred before his prophethood.

Core Idea
Adam's sin was before prophethood, so it does not affect his infallibility as a prophet.

In this part of his commentary, al-Jurjani addresses two key objections that accuse Adam of committing a major sin. He responds by clarifying the timeline: the events of the Garden took place before Adam was chosen as a prophet, as indicated by the word 'thumma' in the Qur'an. This lesson will explain the objections and the core argument that refutes them.

Guided Path
1
Read the objections
Carefully read the fifth and sixth objections based on Qur'anic verses. Note the claim that these verses prove a major sin.
The objections rely on Adam's own words and the expulsion.
2
Identify the response
Find the main response that the sin occurred before prophethood. Look for the word 'thumma' (then) in Surah Ta-Ha.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why timing matters for prophetic infallibility. The passage argues that sins before prophethood are not prohibited.

( الخامس : قوله تعالى : ( حكاية عنهما ( ربنا ظلمنا أنفسنا وإن لم تغفر لنا وترحمنا لنكونن من الخاسرين ﴾ [الأعراف : ۲۳] ، والظلم ذنب كما مر آنفا والخسران لولا المغفرة دليل كونه كبيرة (السادس : قوله تعالى فأزلهما الشيطان عنها فأخرجهما مما كانا فيه ﴾ [البقرة : ٣٦] واستحقاق الإخراج بسبب إزلال الشيطان يدل على كون الصادر عنهما كبيرة . قوله : ( ولا أمة له ) هناك هذا جملة معترضة وخبر أن قوله كان نبياً وفيه بحث وهو أن قوله تعالى : اسكن أنت وزوجك الجنة وكلا منهما رغداً حيث شئتما ولا تقربا هذه الشجرة [البقرة : ٣٥] يدل على أنه أوحي إليه قبل خروجه من الجنة فيدل على نبوته عليه السلام فيها لا يقال : الوحي لا يستلزم النبوة لقوله تعالى : وأوحينا إلى أم موسى أن أرضعيه ﴾ [القصص : أن المرأة لا يتصور نبوتها لأنا نقول : المفهوم مما ورد في حق آدم عليه السلام من الآيات هو إسماع الكلام المنظوم في اليقطة وهو المسمى بالوحي الظاهر، والوحي المتلو ولم يثبت ذلك لغير النبي بل ربما جعل ذلك من خواص الرسول وأما إلقاء المعنى في الروع في اليقظة أو إسماع الكلام في المنام ويقال له الوحي والإيحاء لغة وهو المراد بما ورد في حق أم موسى عليه السلام على ما صرح به في كتب التفسير فغير مختص به قطعا . وأما أنه ليس له أمة في الجنة فقد يجاب عنه بأن حواء أمة له ورد بأن الإرسال إلى الواحد غير معهود ، ولذا قالوا في تعريف النبي : هو من قال له الله تعالى : أرسلناك إلى الناس أو إلى قوم كذا ويمكن أن يدفع بأن غير المعهود هو الإرسال إلى الواحد فقط . والتعريف المذكور لا يقتضي كون الناس المرسل إليهم موجودا في ابتداء الإرسال . إذ لا شك أن البعض الذي يولدون بعد الإرسال يدخلون فيه قطعا. فآدم عليه السلام يجوز أن يكون مرسلاً إلى حواء وبنيها ويكون الموجود في ابتداء الإرسال هو حواء فقط، لكن قال في لباب الأربعين : لو كان آدم عليه السلام رسولاً قبل الواقعة لكان رسولاً من غير مرسل إليه لأنه لم يكن في الجنة بشر سوى حواء وكان الخطاب لها بدون واسطة آدم عليه السلام لقوله تعالى : ولا تقربا ﴾ [البقرة : ٣٥] ، والملائكة رسل الله فلا يحتاجون إلى رسول آخر وأنت خبير بأن ما ذكره يدل على أن الوحي المذكور يستلزم النبوة مع أنهم صرحوا بأن نبوته عليه السلام ثبتت بالكتاب فكان الأقرب أن الخطاب بلا واسطة مع آدم عليه السلام، وأما قوله تعالى: ﴿ ولا تقربا [ البقرة : ٣٥]، فعلى طريق التغليب كما تقرر في المعاني والله أعلم .
Sin. (Fifth: His statement, the Most High: (narrating from both of them: 'Our Lord, we have wronged ourselves, and if You do not forgive us and have mercy upon us, we will surely be among the losers' [Al-A'raf: 23]. And wrongdoing is a sin as previously mentioned, and loss without forgiveness indicates it being a major sin. (Sixth: His statement, the Most High: 'Then Satan caused them to slip therefrom and brought them out from what they were in' [Al-Baqarah: 36]. And deserving of expulsion due to Satan's slipping indicates that what issued from them was a major sin. (We said: (in response) How can it be claimed that he was in paradise and he had no nation) there (was a prophet) sent to convey rulings? (And was the selection for prophethood except after that story?) as indicated by His statement, the Most High: 'So he (Adam) disobeyed his Lord and erred. Then his Lord chose him, and turned to him in forgiveness and guided [him]' [Ta-Ha: 121-122]. For the word 'thumma' (then) indicates delay, and [the story] was before prophethood. (And is the attack) i.e., disparagement (against the prophets with such a weak argument that is obviously refutable except) due to blindness, confusion in error, and extreme ignorance in misguidance.

Then his statement: 'And he has no nation' there: this is an interpolated sentence, and the predicate of 'that' is 'he was a prophet', and there is discussion in it. And it is that His statement, the Most High: 'Dwell, you and your wife, in Paradise and eat from it in ease wherever you wish, but do not approach this tree' [Al-Baqarah: 35] indicates that revelation came to him before his exit from Paradise, thus indicating his prophethood therein. It cannot be said: Revelation does not necessitate prophethood due to His statement, the Most High: 'And We inspired to the mother of Moses to nurse him' [Al-Qasas: 7] because a woman cannot be a prophet. For we say: What is understood from the verses concerning Adam, peace be upon him, is the hearing of constructed speech while awake, which is called apparent revelation and recited revelation, and that is not established for other than a prophet. Rather, that is sometimes made a particularity of the messenger. As for casting the meaning into the heart while awake or hearing speech in a dream, it is called 'wahi' and 'eeha' linguistically, and that is what is meant by what came concerning the mother of Moses, peace be upon him, as clarified in books of tafsir, and it is not specific to a prophet at all. As for his not having a nation in Paradise, it can be answered that Eve is his nation. It was objected that sending to a single person is unprecedented. Hence they said in the definition of a prophet: He is one to whom Allah says: 'We have sent you to the people' or 'to such-and-such a people'. It can be refuted by saying that what is unprecedented is sending to a single person only, and the mentioned definition does not require that the people to whom he is sent exist at the beginning of the sending. For there is no doubt that those who are born after the sending are included in it definitely. So Adam, peace be upon him, could have been sent to Eve and her children, and the only one existing at the beginning of the sending was Eve. But he said in Lubab al-Arba'in: If Adam had been a messenger before the incident, he would have been a messenger with no one sent to, because there was no human in Paradise other than Eve, and the address was to her without the mediation of Adam, peace be upon him, due to His statement: 'And do not approach' [Al-Baqarah: 35], and the angels are messengers of Allah, so they do not need another messenger. And you are aware that what he mentioned indicates that the mentioned revelation necessitates prophethood, while they stated that his prophethood was established by the Book. So the closer [view] is that the address without mediation was with Adam, peace be upon him. As for His statement: 'And do not approach' [Al-Baqarah: 35], it is by way of predominance (taghleeb) as established in semantics. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is a theological defence of the infallibility of prophets, specifically addressing objections regarding Prophet Adam. It begins by presenting the fifth and sixth objections: that the verses where Adam says 'We have wronged ourselves' and where Satan caused their slip indicate that their sin was a major sin (kabira). The response (qulna) is that the story occurred before Adam's prophethood, as indicated by the word 'thumma' (then) in Surah Ta-Ha. Therefore any sin committed was before prophethood and does not affect his infallibility after being chosen. The author then elaborates on the nature of revelation (wahi) to defend the idea that Adam received revelation in Paradise, distinguishing between apparent revelation (al-wahi al-zahir) which is specific to prophets, and inner inspiration (ilqa' al-ma'na fi al-raw') which is general. The discussion continues with whether Adam had a nation (ummah) in Paradise, concluding that it was possible he was sent to Eve, though some (like Lubab al-Arba'in) object that sending to one person is unprecedented. The passage ends by affirming that the best view is that Allah addressed Adam directly before the incident, and the phrase 'do not approach' is by way of predominance (taghleeb).

إزلال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets cannot sin at any point in their lives, even before prophethood.
Correction: Sins before prophethood are not prohibited, as they do not affect a prophet's infallibility after being chosen.

Checkpoint
What is the main reason given in the response for why the objections about Adam's sin are invalid?
A) The sin was not a sin but a mistake.
B) The sin occurred before Adam's prophethood.
C) The sin was forgiven immediately.
D) The sin was not committed by Adam but by Eve alone.

Key Takeaway
Adam's sin in Paradise occurred before his prophethood, so it does not tarnish his prophetic infallibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have surely committed sins before you truly understood your faith. Does that mean you are disqualified from being a good Muslim now? How does Adam's story—sin before prophethood—give you hope that Allah can still choose you for good after your mistakes? What one step will you take today to move forward in faith despite your past?
?
The author says only a blind and ignorant person would attack prophets with such a weak argument. Are there any areas of your life where you hold onto weak or shallow criticisms of Islam or religious teachings out of pride or laziness? Will you commit to honestly investigating those doubts this week?
?
Adam's sin was followed by forgiveness and then elevation to prophethood. Do you truly believe that your worst sins can be forgiven and that you can still be used by Allah for something great? What sin from your past are you still holding onto as if it defines you? How can you let go and trust in Allah's mercy today?
