Refuting the Gharaniq Incident: Satanic Interpolation
Presents the objection and the satanic interpolation answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the first answer to the Gharaniq story preserves the Prophet's infallibility by attributing the offending words to Satanic interpolation.

Core Idea
The Prophet never uttered the praise of idols; Satan mixed his voice with the recitation.

The Gharaniq story is often used to challenge prophetic infallibility. In this passage, the theologian presents the objection and then offers the primary defense: the words were not recited by the Prophet but were thrown onto his tongue by Satan. This explanation maintains the Prophet's sinlessness while accounting for the reported incident.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection narrative
Read the full account of the Gharaniq incident as reported by critics. Note how the story describes the Prophet's distress and the alleged insertion of verses.
The narrative is presented as an objection to prophetic infallibility.
2
Identify the first answer
Focus on the key phrase 'من إلقاء الشيطان'. Understand that the answer claims Satan recited the phrase and mixed his voice with the Prophet's.
This preserves the Prophet from actually uttering falsehood.
3
Reflect on the necessity of this defense
Consider why the theologian emphasizes that if the Prophet had recited the words, it would be disbelief—impermissible by consensus.
The defense upholds the doctrine of 'isma (infallibility).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : ما روي أنه ( عليه الصلاة والسلام لما اشتد عليه إعراض قومه عن دينه تمنى أن يأتيه من الله ما يتقرب به إليهم ويستميل قلوبهم فأنزل الله عليهم سورة والنجم، فلما اشتغل بقراءتها ( قرأ بعد قوله تعالى : أفرأيتم اللات والعزى ﴾ [ النجم : ١٩]، ومناة الثالثة الأخرى تلك الغرانيق العلى منها الشفاعة ترتجى ( فلما سمعه قريش فرحوا به وقالوا : قد ذكر الهتنا بأحسن الذكر ( فأتاه جبريل ( عليه السلام بعدما أمسى ( وقال ) له ( تلوت على الناس ما لم أتله عليك ) ، فحزن النبي لذلك حزناً شديداً الله خوفاً عظيماً ( فنزل ) لتسليته ( وما أرسلنا من قبلك من رسول ولا نبي إلا إذا تمنى ألقى الشيطان في أمنيته إلخ والجواب على تقدير حمل التمني على القراءة هو ( أنه من إلقاء الشيطان ( يعني أن الشيطان قرأ هذه العبارة المنقولة وخلط صوته بصوت النبي ( حتى ظن أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قرأها وإلا ) أي وإن يكن من إلقائه بل ( كان ) النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام قارئالها كان ( ذلك كفراً صادراً عنه وليس بجائز إجماعاً ) وأيضاً ربما كان ما ذكر من العبارات (قرآناً وتكون الإشارة بتلك الغرانيق إلى الملائكة فنسخ تلاوته للإيهام أي لإيهامه المشركين أن المراد به آلهتهم ) أو (المراد على تقدير حمل أتمنى شيئاً وسوس إليه الشيطان ودعاه إلى ما لا ينبغي ثم إن الله تعالى ينسخ ذلك ويهديه إلى ترك الالتفات إلى وسوسته، وعلى هذا تكون الرواية المذكورة من مفتريات الملاحدة (أو) نقول عن التقدير الأول أيضاً ( هو ) أي قوله تلك الغرانيق إلى آخره كان من القرآن وأريد بالغرانيق الأصنام لكنه ) استفهام إنكار) حذف منه أداته فالمعنى أن هذه المستحقرات ليست كما تدعونها وترجون الشفاعة منها .
The second [objection]: What is narrated that when the Prophet (peace be upon him) was distressed by his people's turning away from his religion, he wished that God would send him something by which he could draw near to them and win their hearts. Then God revealed to them Surat al-Najm. When he began reciting it, after His saying: 'Have you considered al-Lat and al-Uzza?' (Quran 53:19), and Manat, the third, the other? 'Those are the high gharaniq (cranes), from them intercession is hoped.' When Quraysh heard that, they rejoiced and said: 'He has mentioned our gods in the best way.' Then Gabriel came to him after evening and said: 'You have recited to the people what I did not bring to you.' So the Prophet became extremely sorrowful and feared greatly. Then was revealed to console him: 'And We did not send before you any messenger or prophet but when he desired, Satan threw into his desire' etc. The answer, on the assumption that 'desire' means recitation, is that it is from Satan's throwing (i.e., Satan recited that transmitted phrase and mixed his voice with the Prophet's voice) until it was thought that the Prophet had recited it. Otherwise (i.e., if the Prophet had actually recited it), that would be disbelief issuing from him, and it is not permissible by consensus. Also, perhaps those expressions were (originally) Quran, and the reference by 'gharaniq' was to angels, but its recitation was abrogated to give the illusion (to the polytheists that their gods were meant). Or, on the assumption that 'desire' was something else, Satan whispered to him and called him to something improper, then God abrogates that and guides him to disregard the whisper. On this basis, the mentioned narration is a fabrication of the atheists. Or, we say regarding the first interpretation as well: his saying 'those are the high gharaniq' to the end was from the Quran, and by 'gharaniq' were meant the idols, but it is a rhetorical question whose interrogative particle was deleted; so the meaning is that these despised things are not as you claim and you hope for intercession from them.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage deals with the contentious 'Gharaniq' story, an objection to the Prophet's infallibility. The objection states that the Prophet, wishing to win over Quraysh, recited verses praising their idols. The answer provides multiple defenses: First, that the words were not recited by the Prophet but thrown by Satan onto his tongue, so the Prophet did not actually utter them. If he had, it would be kufr, which is impermissible for prophets. Second, those words might have been genuine Quran referring to angels, later abrogated to test the polytheists. Third, the narration itself might be a fabrication by heretics. Fourth, the verse might be a rhetorical question rejecting the polytheists' claim. The passage thus comprehensively refutes the story to preserve the Prophet's sinlessness.

Key Terms
إلقاء الشيطان
الغرانيق
عصمة الأنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some claim that the Prophet intentionally praised idols to win over Quraysh, which would violate his infallibility.
Correction: The Prophet did not utter those words; Satan interjected them without the Prophet's awareness, as stated in the answer.

Checkpoint
According to the first answer, how did the offending words enter the recitation?
A) The Prophet recited them deliberately.
B) Gabriel commanded him to recite them.
C) Satan recited them and mixed his voice with the Prophet's.
D) The words were part of the original revelation but later abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The primary defense of the Gharaniq incident is that Satan interpolated the words, not the Prophet, thus maintaining prophetic infallibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After reading this lesson, do you truly believe that the Prophet never faltered in conveying the message, even for a moment? If a part of you doubts, what does that doubt reveal about your trust in Allah's protection of the revelation?
?
The Prophet was deeply grieved when he thought he had recited something wrong. Have you ever been grieved by a mistake in your own worship or speech about Allah? How does that grief move you to be more careful with what you say about your faith?
?
If Satan could mix his voice with the Prophet's recitation without the Prophet knowing, how much more subtle are the deceptions in your own heart? What steps will you take today to guard your tongue and your recitation against the whisperings of the accursed?

Alternative Explanations for the Gharaniq Incident
Offers three alternative defenses for the Gharaniq incident.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three additional responses to the Gharaniq story: abrogation, fabrication, and rhetorical question.

Core Idea
The Gharaniq verses were either genuine Quran abrogated, a heretic fabrication, or a rhetorical question.

Beyond the primary answer of satanic interpolation, scholars provided further defenses to address the Gharaniq story from every angle. These alternatives—abrogation, fabrication, and rhetorical question—each reinforce the doctrine of prophetic infallibility by showing how the story cannot be taken at face value.

Guided Path
1
Understand the abrogation explanation
Read the argument that the phrases might have been original Quran referring to angels, but their recitation was abrogated to test the polytheists.
This preserves the words as divine but later removed.
2
Examine the fabrication claim
Note the suggestion that the entire narration is a fabrication by atheists (ملاحدة). This dismisses the story entirely.
3
Analyze the rhetorical question interpretation
See how the phrase can be read as a rhetorical question denying the polytheists' claims, with the interrogative particle omitted.
This turns the apparent praise into a refutation.

The second [objection]: What is narrated that when the Prophet (peace be upon him) was distressed by his people's turning away from his religion, he wished that God would send him something by which he could draw near to them and win their hearts. Then God revealed to them Surat al-Najm. When he began reciting it, after His saying: 'Have you considered al-Lat and al-Uzza?' (Quran 53:19), and Manat, the third, the other? ?

?

Answer to the Objection of Zayd's Marriage
Defends the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab as a divine command to abrogate custom.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab was a divine command to abrogate the pre-Islamic prohibition of marrying the wives of adopted sons.

Core Idea
The Prophet married Zaynab by God's command, not desire.

This lesson addresses a common objection against the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab. Critics claimed he acted out of personal desire, but the divine answer reveals a deeper purpose: to abrogate a pre-Islamic custom. Let's examine the passage.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Let the author's words sink in.
Notice the flow from objection to answer.
2
Identify the objection and answer
The passage begins with 'The third [objection]' and then gives the answer. Find the core claim of the objection and how the answer refutes it.
The answer uses 'بل كان بأمر الله' implicitly.
3
Understand abrogation (نسخ)
The key term نسخ refers to the abrogation of a previous ruling. Here, God abrogates the pre-Islamic prohibition of marrying the wives of adopted sons.
This explains why the marriage was permissible and even commanded.
4
Reflect on the Prophet's concealment
The verse 33:37 mentions the Prophet's initial hesitation. The passage explains it was out of fear of hypocrites' criticism, not sin.
This preserves the Prophet's infallibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثالث : قصة زيد وزينب والجواب : أنه أي نکاح زينب كان بأمر الله تعالى لنسخ ما كان في الجاهلية من تحريم أزواج الأدعياء وإنما أخفى في نفسه ذلك خوفاً من طعن المنافقين، وتوضيحه أن الله تعالى لما أراد أن ينسخ ذلك التحريم أوحى إليه أن زيداً إذا طلق زوجته فتزوج بها.
The third [objection]: The story of Zayd and Zaynab. The answer: That (i.e., the marriage to Zaynab) was by the command of God Almighty to abrogate what was in the pre-Islamic period of the prohibition of the wives of adopted sons. He only concealed that in himself out of fear of the reproach of the hypocrites. Its clarification is that when God intended to abrogate that prohibition, He revealed to him that when Zayd divorces his wife, he should marry her.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage addresses the objection concerning the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab, the divorced wife of his adopted son Zayd. The objection claims that the Prophet acted out of personal desire. The answer states that this marriage was commanded by God to abrogate the pre-Islamic custom that considered the wife of an adopted son like a biological daughter-in-law, forever forbidden. The Prophet's initial concealment of his intention was out of concern for the hypocrites' criticism, not sin. The explanation continues that God revealed the command in advance, instructing the Prophet to marry Zaynab after Zayd divorced her, thus establishing the new ruling.

Key Terms
نسخ
أزواج الأدعياء
عصمة الأنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet married Zaynab out of personal desire.
Correction: The marriage was commanded by God to abrogate the pre‑Islamic prohibition of marrying the wives of adopted sons.

Checkpoint
Why did the Prophet marry Zaynab according to the answer?
A) Out of love for Zaynab despite societal norms.
B) To follow the pre-Islamic custom of adopted sons' wives.
C) By God's command to abrogate the pre-Islamic prohibition.
D) To strengthen ties with Zayd's family.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's marriage to Zaynab was a divine command to abrogate a pre‑Islamic custom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever known God's command clearly but hesitated to act because you feared what people would say? What would it take for you to obey God even when it invites criticism from hypocrites or society?
?
The Prophet concealed his intention not out of sin, but to shield the truth from those who would distort it. Is there an area of your life where you have concealed your Islamic commitment out of fear? How can you align your inner conviction with your outer actions starting today?
?
This passage shows that God abrogates customs that oppose His law. What deeply ingrained habit or social custom in your life contradicts God's command? Will you ask God for the strength to break it and follow His guidance, even if it feels difficult?

The Gharaniq Incident: Objection and Answers
Al-Iji presents the second objection and gives multiple answers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the various answers given by Sunni scholars to the objection of the 'gharaniq' incident and how they defend prophetic infallibility.

Core Idea
The Prophet never uttered words of shirk; the incident is explained through Satanic interference or abrogated revelation.

The story of the 'gharaniq' (the so-called Satanic verses) is one of the most famous objections against prophetic infallibility. Al-Iji presents this objection and then provides a series of answers that preserve the Prophet's 'isma. This passage shows how kalam scholars handle problematic historical reports by offering multiple plausible interpretations.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Understand the story that was narrated about the Prophet's recitation of Surah an-Najm and the alleged praise of idols. Note the key elements: the Prophet's wish, the recitation, the reaction of Quraysh, and Gabriel's reprimand.
The objection is based on a report that seems to contradict prophetic infallibility.
2
Identify the main answers
The passage gives several answers: 1) Satanic casting (Satan spoke and mixed his voice), 2) The words were originally Quran about angels but recitation was abrogated, 3) The report is a fabrication, 4) It is a rhetorical question denying the idols' status. Note each one.
These answers are not mutually exclusive; they are alternative interpretations.
3
Examine the key terms
The passage explains words like 'gharaniq' and the idols al-Lat, al-Uzza, Manat. Understanding these clarifies the arguments, especially the rhetorical question interpretation.
Lexical analysis shows that 'gharaniq' can refer to water birds or metaphorical delicate beings, not necessarily idols.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني : ما روي أنه ( عليه الصلاة والسلام ) لما اشتد عليه إعراض قومه عن دينه تمنى أن يأتيه من الله ما يتقرب به إليهم ويستميل قلوبهم فأنزل الله عليه سورة والنجم، فلما اشتغل بقراءتها قرأ بعد قوله تعالى : { أفرأيتم اللات والعزى * ومناة الثالثة الأخرى } تلك الغرانيق العلى منها الشفاعة ترتجى. فلما سمعه قريش فرحوا به وقالوا : قد ذكر آلهتنا بأحسن الذكر. فأتاه جبريل ( عليه السلام ) بعدما أمسى وقال له : تلوت على الناس ما لم أتله عليك. فحزن النبي لذلك حزناً شديداً وخاف من الله خوفاً عظيماً. فنزل لتسليته { وما أرسلنا من قبلك من رسول ولا نبي إلا إذا تمنى ألقى الشيطان في أمنيته } الآية. والجواب على تقدير حمل التمني على القراءة هو أنه من إلقاء الشيطان يعني أن الشيطان قرأ هذه العبارة المنقولة وخلط صوته بصوت النبي حتى ظن أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قرأها. وإلا أي وإن يكن من إلقائه بل كان النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام قارئاً لها كان ذلك كفراً صادراً عنه وليس بجائز إجماعاً. وأيضاً ربما كان ما ذكر من العبارات قرآناً وتكون الإشارة بتلك الغرانيق إلى الملائكة فنسخت تلاوته للإيهام أي لإيهام المشركين أن المراد به آلهتهم. أو المراد على تقدير حمل التمني شيئاً وسوس إليه الشيطان ودعاه إلى ما لا ينبغي ثم إن الله تعالى ينسخ ذلك ويهديه إلى ترك الالتفات إلى وسوسته، وعلى هذا تكون الرواية المذكورة من مفتريات الملاحدة. أو نقول عن التقدير الأول أيضاً هو أي قوله تلك الغرانيق إلى آخره كان من القرآن وأريد بالغرانيق الأصنام لكنه استفهام إنكار حذف منه أداته فالمعنى أن هذه المستحقرات ليست كما تدعونها وترجون الشفاعة منها. قوله : ( أفرأيتم اللات والعزى ومناة الثالثة الأخرى ) هي أصنام كانت لهم والثالثة والأخرى صفتان للمناة وفائدتهما التأكيد كقوله يطير بجناحيه أو الأخرى من التأخر في الرتبة. قوله : ( تلك الغرانيق العلى ) الغرنيق بضم الغين المعجمة وفتح النون من طير الماء طويل العنق، وإذا وصف به الرجال فواحدة غرنيق وغرنوق بكسر الغين وفتح النون فيهما وغرنوق بالضم وغرائق وهو الثياب الناعم والجمع الغرائق بالفتح والغرانيق والغرنقة.
The second: What is narrated that he (peace and blessings be upon him) when the turning away of his people from his religion became severe upon him, he wished that there would come to him from God something by which he would draw near to them and win their hearts. So God sent down to them Surah an-Najm. When he occupied himself with reciting it, he recited after His statement {Have you considered al-Lat and al-Uzza? and Manat the third other?} 'Those are the high gharaniq; from them intercession is hoped.' When Quraysh heard him, they rejoiced and said: 'He has mentioned our gods with the best mention.' Then Gabriel (peace be upon him) came to him after evening and said to him: 'You recited to the people what I did not bring to you.' So the Prophet grieved severely and feared God greatly. Then there was revealed to comfort him: {And We sent not before you any messenger or prophet except that when he wished, Satan cast into his wish} etc. The answer, upon the assumption that 'wishing' means recitation, is that it was from Satan's casting, meaning that Satan recited this transmitted phrase and mixed his voice with the voice of the Prophet until they thought that he (peace be upon him) had recited it. Otherwise, i.e., if it were not from his casting, but rather the Prophet (peace be upon him) had been reciting it, that would have been disbelief issuing from him, and it is not permissible by consensus. Also, perhaps what was mentioned of the phrases was Quran, and the reference by 'those gharaniq' was to the angels, and its recitation was abrogated for the suggestion, i.e., to suggest to the polytheists that what was meant were their gods. Or, the meaning, upon the assumption that 'wishing' was something that Satan whispered to him and called him to what is not fitting, then God abrogates that and guides him to disregard his whisper, and on this, the mentioned narration is from the fabrications of the heretics. Or we say concerning the first assumption also: that his statement 'those gharaniq' etc. was from the Quran, and by 'gharaniq' idols were meant, but it is an interrogative of denial with its particle omitted, so the meaning is that these despicable things are not as you claim them to be and hope for intercession from them. His statement: {Have you considered al-Lat and al-Uzza? and Manat the third other?} — they were idols that they had, and 'the third' and 'the other' are attributes of Manat, and their benefit is emphasis, like his saying 'it flies with its two wings' or 'the other' indicating lagging in rank. His statement: {Those are the high gharaniq} — al-ghurniq with a damma on the ghayn and a fatha on the noon is a water bird with a long neck, and if it is used to describe men, its singular is ghurniq and ghurnuq with a kasra on the ghayn and a fatha on the noon in both, and ghurnuq with a damma, and ghara'iq meaning soft garments, and the plural is al-ghara'iq with fatha, and al-gharaniq, and al-gharnaqa.
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection against prophetic infallibility, namely the incident of the 'gharaniq' (the so-called Satanic verses), and provides multiple answers. The objection narrates that the Prophet, distressed by his people's rejection, wished for something to win them over. When reciting Surah an-Najm, he supposedly uttered praise of the idols al-Lat, al-Uzza, and Manat, calling them 'high gharaniq' whose intercession is hoped. Quraysh rejoiced, but Gabriel later told the Prophet he had recited something not revealed. The Prophet grieved, and God revealed the verse about Satan casting into the wishes of prophets. The answer first assumes 'wishing' means recitation: Satan cast these words, mixing his voice with the Prophet's, so the Prophet did not actually recite them. If he had recited them, it would be disbelief, which is impossible. Alternatively, perhaps the words were originally Quran referring to angels, but its recitation was abrogated to avoid misleading polytheists. Another answer: 'wishing' means Satan whispered something inappropriate, but God abrogates it and the Prophet ignores it, so the story is a fabrication. Finally, the phrase might be a rhetorical question ('these despicable things are not as you claim'). The gloss then explains the words: 'al-Lat, al-Uzza, Manat' are idols, 'the third other' emphasizes Manat's low rank; 'gharaniq' are water birds or metaphorical for delicate beings; the plural forms are given.

Key Terms
عصمة
غرانيق
إلقاء الشيطان
نسخ التلاوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet actually recited words praising idols and approved of polytheism.
Correction: The Prophet never uttered such words; they were inserted by Satan (who mixed his voice), or the words were part of the Quran but abrogated, or the story is a fabrication, or the phrase is a rhetorical question denying idol worship.

Checkpoint
What is the primary basis of the answer to the gharaniq objection according to this passage?
A) The Prophet never recited the phrase at all; it was Satan who spoke.
B) The phrase was originally from the Quran but was abrogated.
C) The phrase was a rhetorical question denying the idols' status.
D) All of the above are given as possible explanations.

Key Takeaway
Prophetic infallibility is defended by interpreting the gharaniq incident as Satanic interference, abrogated Quranic verses, or a fabricated report, ensuring the Prophet never committed shirk.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
What whispers of shirk have you entertained in your heart to please others, and how can the Prophet's protection in this incident remind you to immediately reject them and seek refuge in Allah?
?
If Allah protected the Prophet's very recitation, what does that imply about your own responsibility to guard what you say and believe? Examine one area where you dilute faith to fit in – will you rely on Allah's protection and speak truth, or continue compromising?
?
The Prophet feared Allah greatly when he thought he had recited incorrectly. When was the last time you feared displeasing Allah more than the reaction of people? What change will you make today to prioritize divine approval over human praise?

The Third Objection: Zayd and Zaynab – Two Exonerating Explanations
Al-Iji presents two exonerating explanations for the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main explanations that exonerate the Prophet from any sin in his marriage to Zaynab.

Core Idea
The Prophet's marriage to Zaynab was a divine abrogation, not a personal desire.

The story of Zayd and Zaynab has been used as an objection against prophetic infallibility. Critics claim the Prophet acted improperly. Al-Iji presents two exonerating explanations: the first emphasizes the divine command to abrogate a pre-Islamic custom, and the second highlights Zaynab's own actions. Both views affirm the Prophet's innocence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation to get the flow of the two explanations.
2
Identify the two explanations
Find where the first answer ends and the second begins. Notice the transition 'وقيل'.
3
Understand the role of divine command
Both explanations rely on God's command as the ultimate reason for the marriage.
4
Reflect on the conclusion of innocence
The passage ends with 'لا ذنب للنبي في هذه القصة' – no sin for the Prophet on either view.

Source Text

المرصد الأول - المقصد الخامس : في عصمة الأنبياء ( الثالث : قصة زيد وزينب والجواب : أنه أي نكاح زينب كان بأمر الله تعالى لنسخ ما كان في الجاهلية من تحريم أزواج الأدعياء وإنما أخفى في نفسه ذلك خوفاً من طعن المنافقين. وتوضيحه أن الله تعالى لما أراد أن ينسخ ذلك التحريم أوحى إليه أن زيداً إذا طلق زوجته فتزوج بها. فلما حضر زيد ليطلقها خاف أنه إن طلقها لزمه التزوج بها، ويصير سبباً لطعنهم فيه فقال لزيد : أمسك عليك زوجك وأخفى في نفسه ما أوحى إليه وعزمه على نكاحها فلذلك عوتب، فقيل له : { وتخشى الناس والله أحق أن تخشاه }. وقيل : كانت زينب ابنة عمه النبي عليه السلام وطامعة في تزوجه إياها. فلما خطبها النبي لزيد شق عليها وعلى والديها فنزل قوله : { وما كان لمؤمن ولا مؤمنة إذا قضى الله } الآية فانقادوا كرهاً، وطمعت زينب مع ذلك أن يتزوجها النبي ( عليه الصلاة والسلام ) بعد خلاصها من قيد ذلك النكاح. فنشزت على زيد حتى أعيته فطلقها، فتزوجها النبي بأمر من الله بياناً لذلك النسخ. وعلى هذين القولين لا ذنب للنبي في هذه القصة. وما يقال : إنه أحبها حين رآها فمما يجب صيانة النبي عن مثله وإن صح فميل القلب غير مقدور. ثم القائلون بمحبته إياها منهم من قال : لما حبها حرمت على زوجها وهذا باطل وإلا كان أمره بإمساكها أمراً بالزنا وكان وصفها بكونها زوجاً له كذباً. ومنهم من قال : لم تحرم لكن وجب على الزوج تطليقها قالوا : فيه أي في ميل قلبه إليها وما تفرع عليه ابتلاء الزوج بتطليقها لأن النزول عن الزوجة طلباً لمرضاة الله أمر صعب لا ينقاد له إلا موفق. وابتلاء النبي بالمبالغة في حفظ النظر حذراً عن الخيانة في الوحي بالإخفاء أو التعرض للطعن من الأعداء. قوله : ( وعلى هذين القولين الفرق بين القولين أن الوحي والأمر بالنكاح كان قبل التطليق في الأول، وبعده في الثاني وأن سبب التطليق خصوص القصة والنشوز في الثاني دون الأول. قوله : ( وكان وصفها بكونه زوجاً له كذباً ) فإن قلت : يجوز أن يكون ذلك الوصف باعتبار ما كان أو باعتبار الظاهر أو اعتقاد الزوجين ومثله مجاز شائع لا يكون كذباً لما ذكر في المفتاح وغيره من أن المجاز يفارق الكذب. قلت : هذا إنما يكون مجازاً مفارقاً للكذب لو وجد نصب قرينة مانعة عن إرادة الحقيقة ولم يوجد هاهنا كما لا يخفى. قوله : ( لكن وجب على الزوج تطليقها ) فإن قلت : فعلى هذا يكون الأمر بالإمساك أمراً بترك الواجب. قلت : لعله كان الوجوب موسعاً لا مضيقاً فلا محذور.
The First Observation - Fifth Objective: On the Infallibility of Prophets. (Third: The story of Zayd and Zaynab. The answer: That his marriage to Zaynab was by God's command to abrogate what was in pre-Islamic times of prohibition of the wives of adopted sons. He only hid that in himself for fear of the hypocrites' criticism. Its explanation: When God wanted to abrogate that prohibition, He revealed to him that if Zayd divorced his wife, he should marry her. When Zayd came to divorce her, he feared that if he divorced her, he would be obliged to marry her, and that would become a cause for their criticism. So he said to Zayd: 'Keep your wife,' and hid in himself what had been revealed to him and his resolve to marry her. For that he was reproached, and it was said to him: {You fear people, but God is more deserving that you should fear Him}. And it is said: Zaynab was the Prophet's cousin and hoped to marry him. When the Prophet sought her hand for Zayd, it was hard on her and her parents, so the verse was revealed: {It is not for a believing man or a believing woman, when God has decided} etc., and they submitted unwillingly. Yet Zaynab still hoped that the Prophet would marry her after her release from the bond of that marriage. So she acted defiantly toward Zayd until he was exasperated and divorced her. Then the Prophet married her by command of God to demonstrate that abrogation. On these two views, there is no sin for the Prophet in this story. And what is said: that he loved her when he saw her, it is something from which the Prophet must be exonerated; and if it is true, then inclination of the heart is not within one's power. Then those who say he loved her: some say that when he loved her, she became forbidden to her husband, but this is false, otherwise his command to keep her would have been a command to adultery and his describing her as his wife would be a lie. Others say she was not forbidden, but the husband was obliged to divorce her. They say: in that, i.e., in his heart's inclination toward her and what branched from it, there is a trial for the husband to divorce her, because surrendering one's wife seeking God's pleasure is a difficult matter that only the divinely guided can comply with, and a trial for the Prophet to be extreme in guarding his sight, cautious of betrayal of revelation through concealment or exposing himself to criticism from enemies. His statement: (And on these two views, the difference between the two views is that the revelation and command to marry was before the divorce in the first, and after it in the second, and that the cause of divorce was the specific story and defiance in the second, not the first.) His statement: (And describing her as his wife would be a lie.) If you say: It is permissible for that description to be based on what was, or on appearance, or the belief of the couple, and such common metaphor is not a lie, as mentioned in al-Miftah and others that metaphor differs from lying. I say: This is only metaphor distinct from lying if there exists a contextual clue preventing the intended literal meaning, and it does not exist here, as is obvious. His statement: (But the husband was obliged to divorce her.) If you say: On this, the command to keep her would be a command to neglect an obligation. I say: Perhaps the obligation was expansive, not restrictive, so there is no problem.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage presents the third objection against prophetic infallibility, concerning the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab bint Jahsh after her divorce from Zayd, the Prophet's adopted son. The objection alleges impropriety. The answer offers two main explanations. First: God commanded the marriage to abrogate the pre-Islamic prohibition of marrying the wives of adopted sons. The Prophet hid this command from fear of hypocrites' criticism, which is why he was gently reproached in the verse {You fear people...}. Second: Zaynab was the Prophet's cousin and desired to marry him; when the Prophet arranged her marriage to Zayd, she was reluctant but submitted to God's decree. She then defied Zayd until he divorced her, after which the Prophet married her by divine command. In both views, the Prophet committed no sin. The passage then addresses the claim that the Prophet loved Zaynab: such a notion is to be rejected, but even if true, inclination of the heart is involuntary. Opinions are divided: some say love would make her forbidden to Zayd, but that leads to absurdities (command to adultery, false description). Others say it would oblige Zayd to divorce her, which serves as a trial for both Zayd and the Prophet. The marginal notes further clarify the differences between the two views, defend against accusations of lying when the Prophet called Zaynab 'his wife' (since metaphor requires contextual clues absent here), and assert that the obligation to keep Zayd married was expansive, leaving room for divorce later.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet married Zaynab out of personal desire.
Correction: The passage shows the marriage was by divine command to abrogate a custom, not out of personal desire.

According to the first explanation in the passage, why did the Prophet hide his intention to marry Zaynab?
A) Because he was ashamed.
B) For fear of hypocrites' criticism.
C) Because he wanted to test Zayd.
D) Because the marriage was later abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's marriage to Zaynab was divinely ordained to abrogate a pre-Islamic custom, and he is exonerated from any wrongdoing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Prophet was willing to be reproached for abrogating a social norm to obey God. Is there a custom, peer pressure, or family expectation in your life that contradicts a clear command of God? Will you break it, even if it invites criticism? What concrete step will you take this week?
?
Zaynab submitted unwillingly to God's decree when her desired marriage to the Prophet was not initially granted. Have you ever resented God's plan for you because it crossed your personal wishes? How can you train your heart to submit even when submission is painful, and what is the first act of surrender you need to perform today?

The Love Claim and Its Refutations
Al-Iji refutes the claim that the Prophet loved Zaynab and analyzes its implications.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the arguments regarding the claim that the Prophet loved Zaynab and the refutations of those arguments.

Core Idea
Even if the Prophet loved Zaynab, it was an involuntary inclination, not a sin.

After presenting the exonerating explanations, Al-Iji addresses a further claim: that the Prophet loved Zaynab. He exonerates the Prophet from such a notion, but even if it were true, it would not imply sin. Various opinions are discussed and refuted, including the claim that love would make her forbidden to her husband, and the claim that it would oblige divorce.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the love claim
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the claim and its analysis.
2
Identify the two sub-opinions
Find the two opinions among those who say he loved her: one says she became forbidden, the other says the husband must divorce.
3
Understand the refutation of the first opinion
The first opinion is refuted because it leads to absurdities (command to adultery, lying).
4
Understand the refutation of the second opinion
The second opinion is analyzed as a trial; the marginal note clarifies the obligation was expansive.
5
Note the defense against lying accusation
The description of Zaynab as Zayd's wife is literal, not metaphorical, because no contextual clue exists.

بالإخفاء أو التعرض للطعن من الأعداء. قوله : ( وعلى هذين القولين الفرق بين القولين أن الوحي والأمر بالنكاح كان قبل التطليق في الأول، وبعده في الثاني وأن سبب التطليق خصوص القصة والنشوز في الثاني دون الأول. قوله : ( وكان وصفها بكونه زوجاً له كذباً ) فإن قلت : يجوز أن يكون ذلك الوصف باعتبار ما كان أو باعتبار الظاهر أو اعتقاد الزوجين ومثله مجاز شائع لا يكون كذباً لما ذكر في المفتاح وغيره من أن المجاز يفارق الكذب. قلت : هذا إنما يكون مجازاً مفارقاً للكذب لو وجد نصب قرينة مانعة عن إرادة الحقيقة ولم يوجد هاهنا كما لا يخفى. قوله : ( لكن وجب على الزوج تطليقها ) فإن قلت : فعلى هذا يكون الأمر بالإمساك أمراً بترك الواجب. قلت : لعله كان الوجوب موسعاً لا مضيقاً فلا محذور.
The First Observation - Fifth Objective: On the Infallibility of Prophets. (Third: The story of Zayd and Zaynab. The answer: That his marriage to Zaynab was by God's command to abrogate what was in pre-Islamic times of prohibition of the wives of adopted sons. He only hid that in himself for fear of the hypocrites' criticism. Its explanation: When God wanted to abrogate that prohibition, He revealed to him that if Zayd divorced his wife, he should marry her. When Zayd came to divorce her, he feared that if he divorced her, he would be obliged to marry her, and that would become a cause for their criticism. So he said to Zayd: 'Keep your wife,' and hid in himself what had been revealed to him and his resolve to marry her. For that he was reproached, and it was said to him: {You fear people, but God is more deserving that you should fear Him}. And it is said: Zaynab was the Prophet's cousin and hoped to marry him. When the Prophet sought her hand for Zayd, it was hard on her and her parents, so the verse was revealed: {It is not for a believing man or a believing woman, when God has decided} etc., and they submitted unwillingly. Yet Zaynab still hoped that the Prophet would marry her after her release from the bond of that marriage. So she acted defiantly toward Zayd until he was exasperated and divorced her. Then the Prophet married her by command of God to demonstrate that abrogation. On these two views, there is no sin for the Prophet in this story. And what is said: that he loved her when he saw her, it is something from which the Prophet must be exonerated; and if it is true, then inclination of the heart is not within one's power. Then those who say he loved her: some say that when he loved her, she became forbidden to her husband, but this is false, otherwise his command to keep her would have been a command to adultery and his describing her as his wife would be a lie. Others say she was not forbidden, but the husband was obliged to divorce her. They say: in that, i.e., in his heart's inclination toward her and what branched from it, there is a trial for the husband to divorce her, because surrendering one's wife seeking God's pleasure is a difficult matter that only the divinely guided can comply with, and a trial for the Prophet to be extreme in guarding his sight, cautious of betrayal of revelation through concealment or exposing himself to criticism from enemies. His statement: (And on these two views, the difference between the two views is that the revelation and command to marry was before the divorce in the first, and after it in the second, and that the cause of divorce was the specific story and defiance in the second, not the first.) His statement: (And describing her as his wife would be a lie.) If you say: It is permissible for that description to be based on what was, or on appearance, or the belief of the couple, and such common metaphor is not a lie, as mentioned in al-Miftah and others that metaphor differs from lying. I say: This is only metaphor distinct from lying if there exists a contextual clue preventing the intended literal meaning, and it does not exist here, as is obvious. His statement: (But the husband was obliged to divorce her.) If you say: On this, the command to keep her would be a command to neglect an obligation. I say: Perhaps the obligation was expansive, not restrictive, so there is no problem.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage presents the third objection against prophetic infallibility, concerning the Prophet's marriage to Zaynab bint Jahsh after her divorce from Zayd, the Prophet's adopted son. The objection alleges impropriety. The answer offers two main explanations. First: God commanded the marriage to abrogate the pre-Islamic prohibition of marrying the wives of adopted sons. The Prophet hid this command from fear of hypocrites' criticism, which is why he was gently reproached in the verse {You fear people...}. Second: Zaynab was the Prophet's cousin and desired to marry him; when the Prophet arranged her marriage to Zayd, she was reluctant but submitted to God's decree. She then defied Zayd until he divorced her, after which the Prophet married her by divine command. In both views, the Prophet committed no sin. The passage then addresses the claim that the Prophet loved Zaynab: such a notion is to be rejected, but even if true, inclination of the heart is involuntary. Opinions are divided: some say love would make her forbidden to Zayd, but that leads to absurdities (command to adultery, false description). Others say it would oblige Zayd to divorce her, which serves as a trial for both Zayd and the Prophet. The marginal notes further clarify the differences between the two views, defend against accusations of lying when the Prophet called Zaynab 'his wife' (since metaphor requires contextual clues absent here), and assert that the obligation to keep Zayd married was expansive, leaving room for divorce later.

محبة
ميل القلب
مجاز
نسخ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Prophet's love for Zaynab made her forbidden to Zayd.
Correction: This would lead to absurdities (command to adultery, lying), so it is rejected.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the problem with the opinion that the Prophet's love for Zaynab made her forbidden to Zayd?
A) It contradicts the Qur'an.
B) It would make the command to keep her a command to adultery.
C) Love cannot make someone forbidden.
D) Zaynab was already divorced.

Key Takeaway
Claims about the Prophet's love for Zaynab are either to be rejected or understood as involuntary; the opinions suggesting sin are refuted.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you face a difficult situation where your heart inclines to something you know may be wrong, do you immediately assume it is sinful? How does the principle that ‘inclination of the heart is not within one’s power’ change your perspective on your own struggles?
?
The passage discusses trials for the Prophet and for Zayd. In your life, are you willing to surrender something you love for God's pleasure, even if it is extremely difficult? What holds you back from making that sacrifice?

The Captives of Badr: Reprimand for Leaving the Better
Al-Iji presents the fourth objection about the captives of Badr and clarifies it as a reprimand for leaving the better option.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the incident of the captives of Badr is reconciled with prophetic infallibility as a reproach for leaving what is better, not a sin.

Core Idea
The Prophet's choice of ransom was not a sin but a less optimal option, corrected by divine guidance.

This lesson addresses the fourth objection against prophetic infallibility, which cites the verse 'It is not for a prophet to have captives' as a rebuke of the Prophet Muhammad for taking ransom at Badr. We will explore how scholars interpret this rebuke not as a condemnation of sin, but as a gentle reproach for leaving a more preferred action. The passage provides the key answer and the historical context of the consultation with the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the English translation. Notice the structure: objection, answer, then historical narrative.
The passage is dense; take your time with the translation.
2
Identify the objection and response
Pinpoint the objection: the verse seems to criticize the Prophet for taking captives. Then find the answer: it is a reproach for leaving what is better (al-awla), not a prohibition.
The key phrase is 'عتاب على ترك الأولى'.
3
Reflect on 'leaving what is better'
Consider how this concept protects prophetic infallibility. The Prophet chose a permissible action (ransom) that was less optimal than killing the captives. The divine rebuke guides toward the better choice without implying sin.
Compare the advice of Abu Bakr, Umar, and Sa'd to see different perspectives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرابع : { ما كان لنبي أن يكون له أسرى } إلى قوله { عذاب عظيم } والجواب : أنه عتاب على ترك الأولى الذي هو الإثخان. فإن التحريم أي تحريم الفداء مستفاد من هذه الآية، فقبل نزولها لا تحريم. ومعنى قوله تعالى : { لولا كتاب } [ الأنفال : ٦٨ ] إلى آخر الآية، أنه لولا كتاب من الله سبق بتأخير العذاب عنهم لنالهم عذاب عظيم. وروي أن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام أتي بسبعين أسيراً يوم بدر فيهم العباس عمه وعقيل ابن أبي طالب، واستشار أبا بكر فيهم فقال: قومك وأهلك استبقهم فلعل الله تعالى أن يتوب عليهم وخذ منهم فدية تقوي بها أصحابك. وقال عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه: كذبوك وأخرجوك من بلدك فاضرب أعناقهم. وقال سعد بن معاذ: الإثخان في القتل أحب إلي. فرضي رسول الله عليه السلام بالفداء فنزلت الآية.
Fourth: {It is not for a prophet to have captives} until His saying {a great punishment}. And the answer: It is a reproach for leaving what is better, which is slaughter. For the prohibition, i.e., prohibition of ransom, is derived from this verse, so before its revelation there was no prohibition. And the meaning of His statement {Were it not for a decree} [al-Anfal: 68] to the end of the verse, is that were it not for a decree from God preceding postponing punishment from them, a great punishment would have befallen them. And it is narrated that the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) was brought seventy captives on the day of Badr, among them al-Abbas his uncle and 'Uqayl ibn Abi Talib. He consulted Abu Bakr about them. He said: 'Your people and family, spare them, perhaps God will relent toward them, and take ransom from them to strengthen your companions.' 'Umar (may God be pleased with him) said: 'They denied you and expelled you from your land, so strike their necks.' Sa'd ibn Mu'adh said: 'Slaughter is more beloved to me.' The Messenger of God (peace and blessings be upon him) approved ransom, and the verse was revealed.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth objection against prophetic infallibility, based on the verse {It is not for a prophet to have captives} which seems to rebuke the Prophet for taking ransom from the captives of Badr. The answer is that this is a reproach for leaving what is better (al-awla), not a sin. The better action was to kill the captives (al-ithkhan), but taking ransom was still permissible because the prohibition of ransom was derived from this very verse, meaning before its revelation, ransom was not forbidden. The verse's mention of 'a great punishment' is mitigated by God's prior decree to postpone punishment. The passage then recounts the historical context: the Prophet consulted his companions; Abu Bakr advised taking ransom to strengthen the Muslims, 'Umar advised execution, and Sa'd advised killing. The Prophet chose the ransom, and then the verse was revealed. Thus, the Prophet's choice was not sinful but a less optimal option, and the verse served as divine guidance for the future.

Key Terms
أسرى
فداء
إثخان
عتاب
الأولى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Prophet committed a sin by taking ransom from the captives of Badr.
Correction: The divine rebuke was a reproach for leaving the better option (al-awla), not a sin. The action of taking ransom was permissible before the verse, and the verse itself established the prohibition.

Checkpoint
What does the passage identify as the nature of the divine rebuke in the captives of Badr incident?
A) It was a punishment for a major sin.
B) It was a reproach for leaving what is better, not for a prohibited act.
C) It was a withdrawal of prophecy.
D) It was a test of the Prophet's obedience.

Key Takeaway
The divine rebuke in the captives of Badr incident reproaches the Prophet for choosing a permissible but less optimal action, not for committing a sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone corrects you for choosing a permissible but less good action, do you accept it with humility like the Prophet did, or do you become defensive? Reflect on a recent situation where you could have chosen a better option and ask Allah for guidance to always seek al-awla.
?
The Prophet consulted his companions before deciding. In your important decisions, do you seek sincere counsel, or do you rely solely on your own judgment? Commit today to consult a trusted person before a major choice, following the Prophetic example.
?
The verse says 'were it not for a prior decree, a great punishment would have befallen you.' If Allah held you to the highest standard, would you deserve punishment for your choices? How does this deepen your gratitude for His mercy, and what change will you make in your daily actions?

The Captives of Badr and Prophetic Infallibility
Narrative of the Prophet's decision regarding captives at Badr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the story of the captives of Badr is used as an objection against prophetic infallibility and how it is resolved through the concept of ترك الأولى (the lesser optimal choice).

Core Idea
The Prophet's choice of ransom was not a sin but a lesser optimal choice permitted by divine decree.

The fourth objection to prophetic infallibility comes from the Prophet's handling of the captives at Badr. Critics argue that the verse rebuking the ransom indicates a mistake, but scholars explain it as a matter of ترك الأولى—a permissible but less optimal decision. This lesson unpacks the narrative and its theological resolution.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative
Read the story of the captives and the consultation with Abu Bakr, Umar, and Sa'd.
2
Identify the objection
Notice how the verse could be misread as rebuking the Prophet for a sinful choice.
3
Understand the resolution
Learn why scholars classify this as ترك الأولى, not sin, due to a prior permission.
4
Reflect on infallibility
See how this case fits the broader doctrine that prophets are protected from major and minor sins, but not from lesser optimal choices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (الرابع: ما كان لنبي الآية روي أن النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام أتى بسبعين أسيراً يوم بدر فيهم العباس عمه وعقيل ابن أبي طالب واستشار أبا بكر فيهم، فقال: قومك وأهلك استبقهم فلعل الله تعالى أن يتوب عليهم وخذ منهم فدية تقوي بها أصحابك، وقال عمر رضي الله تعالى عنهم : كذبوك وأخرجوك من بلدك فاضرب أعناقهم، وقال : سعد بن معاذ الإثخان في القتل أحب إلي فرضي رسول الله عليه السلام بالفداء فنزلت الآية . سبق تحليل الغنائم لعذبتكم بسبب أخذكم هذا الفداء
His saying: (The fourth: The Prophet cannot have captives... the verse) It is narrated that the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, was brought seventy captives on the day of Badr, among them al-Abbas his uncle and Aqil ibn Abi Talib. He consulted Abu Bakr about them, who said: 'Your people and family, spare them, perhaps Allah will turn to them [in repentance], and take ransom from them to strengthen your companions.' Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, said: 'They denied you and expelled you from your land, so strike their necks.' Sa'd ibn Mu'adh said: 'Extermination in killing is dearer to me.' The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, was pleased with the ransom, and the verse was revealed: 'Were it not for a prior permission of spoils, He would have punished you for taking this ransom.'
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth objection regarding prophetic infallibility through the narrative of the captives taken at Badr. The Prophet consulted his companions: Abu Bakr recommended mercy and ransom, Umar advocated execution, and Sa'd favored annihilation. The Prophet chose the ransom, after which the verse was revealed indicating that the action was not sinful but a lesser optimal choice (ترك الأولى) because a prior divine decree had already permitted spoils. The passage shows that the Prophet's decision was a matter of worldly judgment, not disobedience.

Key Terms
أسرى
فداء
ترك الأولى
عصمة الأنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse rebuking the ransom indicates the Prophet committed a sin.
Correction: The verse shows that the action was permitted by a prior divine decree, so it was not a sin but a lesser optimal choice.

Checkpoint

B) He released them without ransom

Key Takeaway
The story of the captives of Badr does not contradict prophetic infallibility, as the Prophet's choice was a permissible lesser optimal choice, not a sin.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The verse warns that without prior permission, the Prophet would have been punished. In what areas of your life have you relied on Allah's prior permissions (i.e., clear rulings) to avoid sin? Where might you be acting without such permission, assuming leniency that is not granted?

The Gentle Rebuke: Meaning of 'May Allah Forgive You'
Explanation that the rebuke in 'Afā Allāhu 'anka' is a gentle address, not blame for sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the phrase 'عفا الله عنك' in the Qur'an is a conventional gentle address and not evidence of sin, and how scholars reconcile it with divine forgiveness.

Core Idea
Forgiveness does not imply sin when it is a gentle address.

This lesson addresses a common objection against the Prophet's infallibility based on the verse 'عفا الله عنك لم أذنت لهم'. The scholars explain that this phrase is a form of gentle address, not a statement of forgiveness after sin. We will explore the argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the translation. Note the objection and the immediate answer given.
The answer begins with 'والجواب : أنه تلطف في الخطاب'.
2
Understand 'تلطف في الخطاب'
Grasp the concept of gentle address, comparing it to phrases like 'رحمك الله'. See why it cannot be taken literally.
The scholars argue that taking it literally leads to contradiction: forgiveness after sin followed by rebuke is impossible.
3
Analyze the concession about 'ترك الأولى'
Even if the verse implies a rebuke, it is only for leaving the better option in worldly matters, not a sin.
This preserves the doctrine of 'ismah (infallibility) regarding religious matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( الخامس : عفا الله عنك لم أذنت لهم والجواب : أنه تلطف في الخطاب) على طريقة قولك : أرأيت رحمك الله وغفر لك ولا يمكن إجراؤه على ظاهره الذي هو أنه تعالى عفا عنه ثم عاتبه، إذ هو باطل قطعوا إليه أشار بقوله : ( وإلا فلا عتاب بعد العفو)، وعلى هذا فلا دلالة للعفو على الذنب (و) إن سلم أن هناك عتاباً، (قلنا: ذلك) العتاب إنما كان ) بترك الأولى فيما يتعلق بالمصالح الدنيوية ) من تدبير الحروب فإنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أذن جماعة تعللوا بأعذار بالتخلف عن غزوة تبوك وتارك الأفضل في أمور الحرب قد يعاتب .
(The fifth: 'May Allah forgive you; why did you permit them?' And the answer: It is gentleness in address, following the manner of your saying: 'Do you not see? May Allah have mercy on you and forgive you.' It cannot be taken at face value, that He forgave him and then rebuked him, for that is false as they decisively pointed out by his saying: 'And if so, there is no rebuke after forgiveness.' So there is no indication from forgiveness of sin. And if one concedes that there is rebuke, we say: That rebuke is only for leaving the better option regarding worldly interests of war management, for the Prophet, peace be upon him, permitted a group who made excuses to stay behind from the expedition of Tabuk, and one who leaves the better in matters of war may be rebuked.)
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage addresses the fifth objection based on the verse 'عفا الله عنك لم أذنت لهم' (May Allah forgive you; why did you permit them?). The answer explains that this is a gentle address, similar to saying 'May Allah have mercy on you and forgive you' in Arabic, which is not evidence of actual sin. It cannot mean Allah forgave and then blamed, as that is contradictory. If any rebuke is admitted, it is only for leaving the better option (ترك الأولى) in worldly matters of war strategy, when the Prophet allowed some to stay behind from Tabuk due to their excuses.

Key Terms
عفا الله عنك
تلطف
ترك الأولى
عتاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'عفا الله عنك' shows that the Prophet committed a sin.
Correction: The passage explains it is a conventional gentle address, similar to saying 'may Allah have mercy on you', not indicating actual sin.

Checkpoint
According to the answer, what does the phrase 'عفا الله عنك' in the objection actually signify?
A) Allah truly forgave a sin
B) A gentle address like 'may Allah have mercy on you'
C) A command to punish the hypocrites
D) A decree of forgiveness without any rebuke

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'عفا الله عنك' is a gentle address, not an indication of sin; any rebuke is for leaving the better in worldly matters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When someone gently corrects you with a phrase like 'May Allah forgive you', do you defensively assume they are accusing you of sin, or do you respond with humility, recognizing their kindness? What does your reaction reveal about your heart?

The Prophet was rebuked for leaving the better in a worldly matter. Think of a recent situation where you settled for a lower good when you could have chosen the better. What held you back? Will you commit to striving for excellence even in worldly affairs, seeking Allah's pleasure?
?
How often do you misinterpret the intentions of others because you take their words at face value, without considering context? Is there a relationship in your life that suffers because of such misunderstandings? What step can you take today to repair it?

Interpreting 'Wizr' in Surah al-Sharh
Interpretation of 'wizr' in Surah al-Sharh as burden or pre-prophetic minor sins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three scholarly interpretations of the term 'wizr' in Surah al-Sharh and how each upholds the doctrine of prophetic sinlessness.

Core Idea
The 'burden' removed from the Prophet was grief, not sin.

This lesson addresses a common objection based on the verse 'We removed from you your burden.' Critics claim it implies the Prophet had sins. The passage provides three nuanced interpretations that uphold prophetic infallibility while respecting the Quranic text. Let's examine each one carefully.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and objection
Start by reading the verse and understanding why it might be seen as problematic for the doctrine of 'isma (sinlessness).
2
Examine the first interpretation
The first interpretation suggests 'wizr' refers to minor faults before prophethood, which are not considered sins against the prophetic state.
3
Examine the second interpretation
The second interpretation sees 'wizr' as leaving the better option (tark al-awla), a permissible action that is not sinful.
4
Understand the third interpretation
The third, preferred interpretation takes 'wizr' in its literal meaning of heaviness, referring to the Prophet's grief over his people's rejection.
This is supported by Quranic usage and context.
5
Review the supporting evidence
Notice how the author uses the surrounding verses and linguistic parallels to strengthen the third interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
( السادس : ووضعنا عنك وزرك الذي أنقض ظهرك ) والوزر هو الذنب وإنقاضه الظهر يدل على كبره ( الجواب : ( بأن الوزر المذكور محمول على ما كان قد اقترفه ( قبل النبوة أو ( هو ) ترك الأولى ) والإنقاض حينئذ محمول على استعظامه إياه ، ( أو ) نقول إنه قد جاء بمعنى الثقل كقوله تعالى : حتى تضع الحرب أوزارها ﴾ [محمد : ٤] ، فجاز أن يكون هاهنا مستعملا للثقل الذي كان عليه من الغم الشديد ( لإصرار قومه ) على إنكاره والشرك بالله ولعدم استطاعته على تنفيذ أمر الدين فلما أعلى الله شأنه وشد أزره فقد وضع عنه وزره وثقله ويقوي هذا التأويل قوله تعالى : ورفعنا لك ذكرك [ الشرح : ٤ ]، وقوله : إن مع ) العسر يسراً ﴾ [الشرح : ٦]،
(The sixth: 'And We removed from you your burden which weighed down your back' – and 'wizr' is sin, and weighing down the back indicates its magnitude. The answer: The mentioned wizr is interpreted as what he committed before prophethood, or it is leaving the better option, and the weighing down then is interpreted as his deeming it great. Or we say it has come in the sense of heaviness, as His saying: 'Until war lays down its burdens' [Muhammad: 4]. So it is permissible that it is used here for the heaviness of severe grief due to his people's insistence on denying him and associating partners with Allah, and his inability to implement the religion's command. When Allah elevated his station and strengthened his arm, He removed from him his burden and heaviness. This interpretation is supported by His saying: 'And We raised high your mention' [al-Sharh: 4] and His saying: 'Indeed, with hardship [comes] ease' [al-Sharh: 6].)
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage addresses the sixth objection from the verse 'ووضعنا عنك وزرك الذي أنقض ظهرك' (We removed your burden that weighed down your back). The term 'wizr' is often understood as sin. The answer offers three interpretations: 1) It refers to minor faults before prophethood; 2) It means leaving the better option (ترك الأولى); 3) It means heaviness and grief, as used in the verse about war laying down its burdens. The third interpretation is supported by context: the Prophet's burden was the grief from his people's rejection and the difficulty of his mission. This interpretation is strengthened by the surrounding verses about raising his mention and ease after hardship.

Key Terms
وزر
إنقاض الظهر
ترك الأولى
ثقل
الغم الشديد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse proves that the Prophet committed sins.
Correction: Scholars interpret 'wizr' as either pre-prophetic minor faults, leaving the better option, or metaphorical heaviness, none of which imply sin.

Checkpoint
Which interpretation of 'wizr' does the author support with Quranic evidence from the same surah?
A) It refers to sin before prophethood
B) It means leaving the better option
C) It signifies the burden of grief and hardship
D) It indicates disbelief

Key Takeaway
The verse about removing the burden from the Prophet does not imply sin; rather, it refers to the removal of grief and hardship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
You have just learned that 'wizr' can mean a burden of grief, not sin. Are there any 'burdens' you carry that you mistakenly believe are punishments from Allah? How can you realign your understanding and seek the true meaning of relief from Him?

Prophetic Forgiveness Verses: Three Interpretations
Interpretation of forgiveness verses as referring to ummah's sins or pre-prophetic actions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how classical scholars interpret Quranic verses that mention forgiveness for the Prophet in a way that preserves his infallibility.

Core Idea
Forgiveness verses refer to the ummah's sins or to the Prophet's pre-prophetic minor faults.

This lesson addresses a common objection to prophetic infallibility: verses like 'That Allah may forgive you your sins' (al-Fath 2) seem to imply the Prophet committed sins. The passage provides three alternative interpretations that reconcile these verses with the doctrine of 'isma (infallibility). Each interpretation shifts the referent of 'sin' away from the Prophet's post-prophetic actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and verses
First, read the Quranic verses cited in the objection: al-Fath 2, Ghafir 55, and al-Tawbah 117. Notice that they connect forgiveness or repentance to the Prophet.
The objection is that forgiveness presupposes sin, which contradicts infallibility.
2
Explore the first interpretation
The first answer explains that these verses refer to minor faults that occurred before prophethood. The phrase 'what preceded and what will follow' is taken relative to the time of prophethood.
This interpretation limits any fault to the pre-prophetic period.
3
Understand the second interpretation
The second answer says the term 'sin' here actually means 'leaving the better option' (tark al-awla). Calling it a sin is a magnifying expression to emphasize its inappropriateness for someone of his rank.
This preserves infallibility by redefining 'sin' as a lesser shortcoming.
4
Analyze the third interpretation
The third answer holds that the sins attributed to the Prophet are actually the sins of his community, attributed to him as their leader. The grammatical structure supports this: the verbal noun is added to the object.
This is a common rhetorical device where a leader is associated with followers' actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(السابع قوله : ليغفر لك الله ما تقدم من ذنبك وما تأخر [الفتح : ٢]، و قوله : ( واستغفر لذنبك ﴾ [غافر: ٥٥]، و) قوله : ( لقد ( تاب الله على النبي ﴾ [التوبة : ١١٧ ] ) إذ لا وجود للتوبة إلا مع الذنب، ( الجواب أنه قبل النبوة وحمله على ما تقدم النبوة وما تأخر عنها لادلالة للفظ عليه ) ، إذ يجوز أن يصدر عنه قبل النبوة صغيرتان إحداهما متقدمة على الأخرى ( أو ) أنه ( ترك الأولى ) وتسميته بالذنب استعظام لصدوره عنه ( أو ) نقول : (نسب إليه ذنب قومه ) فإن رئيس القوم قد ينسب إليه ما فعله بعض أتباعه فالمعنى ليغفر لأجلك ما تقدم من ذنب أمتك، وما تأخر منه واستغفر لذنب أمتك وتاب الله على أمة النبيله وأتباعه ( وأما ما يقال أن المصدر مضاف إلى المفعول فالمعنى ذنب قومك إليك )
(The seventh: His saying: 'That Allah may forgive you what preceded of your sin and what will follow' [al-Fath: 2], and His saying: 'And seek forgiveness for your sin' [Ghafir: 55], and His saying: 'Allah has indeed turned in forgiveness to the Prophet' [al-Tawbah: 117] – for repentance only occurs with sin. The answer: It is [understood as] before prophethood, and it is interpreted as what preceded prophethood and what followed it, since there is no indication in the wording [that it is after]. For it is possible that two minor sins occurred before prophethood, one before the other. Or it is leaving the better option, and its being called 'sin' is for magnifying its occurrence from him. Or we say: The sins of his people are attributed to him, for the leader may be attributed with what some of his followers did. So the meaning is: for your sake, forgive what preceded of the sin of your ummah and what will follow, and seek forgiveness for the sin of your ummah, and Allah turned to the ummah of the Prophet and his followers. And as for what is said that the infinitive is added to the object, so the meaning is 'the sin of your people to you'.)
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage addresses the seventh objection, citing three verses that mention forgiveness or repentance for the Prophet. The objection is that forgiveness implies sin. The answer offers three interpretations: 1) The verses refer to pre-prophetic minor faults; 'what precedes and what follows' can be taken relative to the time of prophethood. 2) It means leaving the better option (ترك الأولى), and calling it 'sin' emphasizes its gravity. 3) The sins are attributed to the Prophet because they belong to his community; the leader is associated with his followers' actions. The last interpretation is supported by grammatical analysis: the verbal noun can be taken with object meaning 'your people's sin against you'.

Key Terms
الذنب
المغفرة
التوبة
ترك الأولى
نسبة الذنب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These verses prove that the Prophet committed sins after prophethood.
Correction: Scholars interpret the verses as referring to pre-prophetic minor faults, leaving the better option, or the sins of the ummah attributed to the Prophet.

Checkpoint
According to the third interpretation given for the forgiveness verses, whose sins are being forgiven?
A) The Prophet's own sins
B) The sins of the ummah attributed to the Prophet
C) The sins of the hypocrites
D) The sins of previous prophets

Key Takeaway
Classical scholarship defends prophetic infallibility by reinterpreting forgiveness verses as referring to pre-prophetic actions, leaving the better option, or the sins of the community.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that even the Prophet's 'leaving the better option' is considered a serious matter, do you downplay your own sins by rationalizing them as 'not that bad'? What specific sin will you repent of today because of this lesson?

?

The Tabuk Expedition and the Divine Rebuke
Narrative of the Tabuk expedition and the permission to stay behind.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical circumstances of the fifth objection in the discussion of prophethood, specifically the Tabuk expedition and the revelation of the verse 'عفا الله عنك'.

Core Idea
Even the Prophet's merciful permissions could become occasions for gentle divine correction.

This passage recounts a specific event in the life of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) that is used as an objection in theological discussions. To properly engage with the objection, one must know the story: after a difficult journey, some companions sought permission to stay behind from the Tabuk expedition, and the Prophet granted it, leading to a verse that gently rebuked him. This lesson sets the scene.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the literal translation. Let the narrative flow.
Key terms: غزوة تبوك, التخلف, عسرة
2
Identify the difficult conditions
Notice the three hardships mentioned: hardship (عسرة), drought (قحط), and intense heat (قيظ), along with the distant goal and numerous enemy.
These details are important for understanding why excuses were genuine.
3
Sequence the events
The order: people resolved to go → some sought permission → Prophet heard excuses → permitted them → verse was revealed. Understand each step.
The verse is a gentle rebuke for permitting them.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself: why is this story used as an objection? It shows that even a prophet's action could be corrected, which relates to the doctrine of prophethood.
This connects to the broader theological discussion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (الخامس عفا الله عنك (الآية روي أن رسول الله عليه السلام بعد رجوعه عن الطائف استقر القوم إلى تبوك وكان في وقت عسرة وقحط وقيظ مع بعد المقصد وكثرة العدو، واستأذن طائفة منهم في التخلف واعتلوا بعلل فسمع عليه السلام معاذيرهم وأذن في التخلف فنزلت الآية

A group among them sought permission to stay behind, offering excuses, so he heard their excuses and permitted them to stay behind, so the verse was revealed.

Commentary
This passage provides the historical narrative for the fifth objection. It recounts that after the return from Ta'if, the Muslims prepared for the expedition to Tabuk under difficult conditions: drought, heat, long distance, and strong enemy. Some companions asked permission to remain behind, bringing excuses. The Prophet accepted their excuses and allowed them to stay. The verse 'عفا الله عنك لم أذنت لهم' was then revealed. This story illustrates the context of the gentle rebuke.

Fifth Objection: 'May Allah Forgive You' Verse
Al-Iji presents the fifth objection regarding the verse 'May Allah forgive you' and answers it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the verse 'May Allah forgive you' is interpreted to preserve prophetic infallibility through the concepts of gentle address and leaving what is better.

Core Idea
Forgiveness in the verse is not literal but a gentle address.

The fifth objection argues that the Qur'anic verse 'May Allah forgive you' implies the Prophet committed a sin, since forgiveness is only for sin. This lesson presents Al-Iji's response, which explains that the verse is a form of rhetorical gentle address, or alternatively, a reprimand for leaving a preferable action in worldly matters, not a sin.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the objection that forgiveness only applies to sin, and the initial answer that it is a gentle address.
2
Understand 'talattuf fi al-khitab'
Focus on the explanation that this phrase is like saying 'May Allah have mercy on you' – it is rhetorical, not literal.
This preserves the Prophet's sinlessness.
3
Examine the second interpretation
If we accept a reprimand, it is for 'tark al-awla' (leaving the better) in worldly military strategy, not a moral failure.
4
Learn the historical context
Read the narration about the expedition of Tabuk to see why the verse was revealed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامس : عفا الله عنك لم أذنت لهم والعفو إنما يكون عن الذنب الجواب : أنه تلطف في الخطاب على طريقة قولك : أرأيت رحمك الله وغفر لك ولا يمكن إجراؤه على ظاهره الذي هو أنه تعالى عفا عنه ثم عاتبه، إذ هو باطل قطعوا إليه أشار بقوله : ( وإلا فلا عتاب بعد العفو)، وعلى هذا فلا دلالة للعفو على الذنب (و) إن سلم أن هناك عتاباً، (قلنا: ذلك) العتاب إنما كان ) بترك الأولى فيما يتعلق بالمصالح الدنيوية ) من تدبير الحروب فإنه عليه الصلاة والسلام أذن جماعة تعللوا بأعذار بالتخلف عن غزوة تبوك وتارك الأفضل في أمور الحرب قد يعاتب . و قوله : (الخامس عفا الله عنك (الآية روي أن رسول الله عليه السلام بعد رجوعه عن الطائف استقر القوم إلى تبوك وكان في وقت عسرة وقحط وقيظ مع بعد المقصد وكثرة العدو، واستأذن طائفة منهم في التخلف واعتلوا بعلل فسمع عليه السلام معاذيرهم وأذن في التخلف فنزلت الآية، وأما عاقبة الله الله سبحانه مع اعتذارهم ! هم إليه عليه السلام لأنه كان عليه أن يتفحص عن کنه معاذيرهم فقصر في ذلك
The fifth: 'May Allah forgive you, why did you give them permission?' and forgiveness is only for sin. The answer: It is a gentle address in speech, like your saying: 'Do you see, may Allah have mercy on you and forgive you,' and it cannot be taken at its apparent meaning which is that He, exalted, forgave him then reprimanded him, for that is false. He indicated by His saying: 'Otherwise there is no reprimand after forgiveness.' And upon this, forgiveness does not indicate sin. And if it is conceded that there is a reprimand, we say: That reprimand was only for leaving what is better regarding worldly interests, such as the management of wars. Indeed, he, peace be upon him, gave permission to a group who made excuses to stay behind from the expedition of Tabuk, and one who leaves the better in matters of war may be reprimanded. And His saying: 'The fifth: May Allah forgive you' (the verse) — it is narrated that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, after his return from Ta'if, the people set out for Tabuk during a time of hardship, drought, and heat, with a distant destination and many enemies. A group among them asked permission to stay behind and pleaded excuses. He, peace be upon him, heard their excuses and gave permission for them to stay behind, then the verse was revealed. And as for the consequence — Allah, exalted be He, with their excuse they?! to him, peace be upon him, because it was incumbent upon him to investigate the essence of their excuses, and he fell short in that.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. Al-Iji presents the fifth objection that the Qur'anic verse 'May Allah forgive you' implies the Prophet committed a sin, since forgiveness is only for sin. The answer explains that this is a form of gentle address (talattuf fi al-khitab), similar to the rhetorical 'May Allah have mercy on you' which does not imply actual sin. A second interpretation is that even if the verse is a reprimand, it concerns leaving a preferable action (tark al-awla) in worldly military strategy, not a sin. The supporting narration recounts the background of the expedition of Tabuk, where the Prophet allowed some people to stay behind due to their excuses, which was a less optimal decision but not sinful.

Key Terms
عصمة الأنبياء
عفا الله عنك
تلطف في الخطاب
عتاب
ترك الأولى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'عفا الله عنك' proves the Prophet committed a sin.
Correction: The verse is a gentle address or a reprimand for leaving what is better, not a sin.

Checkpoint
According to the answer to the fifth objection, what does the verse 'عفا الله عنك' indicate?
A) The Prophet committed a sin.
B) It is a form of gentle address, not literal forgiveness.
C) The Prophet abandoned a religious obligation.
D) The verse was abrogated.

Key Takeaway
The verse 'May Allah forgive you' is not a proof of sin; it is either a rhetorical gentle address or a reprimand for leaving a preferable worldly action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The Prophet was reprimanded for not investigating excuses thoroughly. In your own life, when you accept someone's excuse, do you investigate enough? Or do you fall short like the Prophet did, yet without his innocence? What will you do differently tomorrow?
